            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom) at ($(ctdcQuarterLeftTop)!0.875!(ctdcQuarterLeftBottom)$);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTop) -- (ctdcQuarterLeftTapTop);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapTop) to[currtap, name=ctdcquarterleft] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom) -- (ctdcQuarterLeftBottom);
            \coordinate (focCurrSenseInA) at ($(foc.south east)!0.2!(foc.south west)$);
            \coordinate (focCurrSenseInB) at ($(foc.south east)!0.4!(foc.south west)$);
            \coordinate (focCurrSenseInC) at ($(foc.south east)!0.6!(foc.south west)$);
            \coordinate (focPllSenseIn) at ($(foc.south west)!0.2!(foc.south east)$);
            \coordinate (pllWestThird) at ($(pll.south west)!0.666!(pll.north west)$);
            \coordinate (pllWestBelow) at ($(pll.south west)!0.333!(pll.north west)$);
            \coordinate (pwmDropA) at (pwm.south |- ctdcquarter.tap);
            \coordinate (pwmDropB) at (pwm.south |- ctdc.tap);
            \coordinate (pwmDropC) at (pwm.south |- ctdcquarterleft.tap);
            \coordinate (pwmModBusLevel) at ($(ctdcquarterleft.tap)+(0,-0.18)$);
            \coordinate (pwmModBusStart) at (pwm.south |- pwmModBusLevel);
            \coordinate (pwmModBusEnd) at (mod.east |- pwmModBusLevel);
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpPwmDropA, thick] at (pwmDropA) {};
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpPwmDropB, thick] at (pwmDropB) {};
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpPwmDropC, thick] at (pwmDropC) {};

            \draw[thick, ->] (ctdcquarter.tap) -| (focCurrSenseInA);
            \draw[thick, ->] (ctdc.tap) -| (focCurrSenseInB);
            \draw[thick, ->] (ctdcquarterleft.tap) -| (focCurrSenseInC);
            \draw[thick, ->] (pllWestThird) -| (focPllSenseIn);
            \draw[thick, ->] (pllWestBelow) -| (mod.south);
            \draw[thick] (pwm.south) -- (jumpPwmDropA.west);
            \draw[thick] (jumpPwmDropA.east) -- (jumpPwmDropB.west);
            \draw[thick] (jumpPwmDropB.east) -- (jumpPwmDropC.west);
            \draw[thick, siglabel, ->] (jumpPwmDropC.east) |- node[pos=0.96, above] {$m$} (mod.east);
            \node[siglabel, above] at (sALabelPos |- ctdcquarter.tap) {$i_\mathrm{a}$};
            \node[siglabel, above] at (sBLabelPos |- ctdc.tap) {$i_\mathrm{b}$};
            \node[siglabel, above] at (sCLabelPos |- ctdcquarterleft.tap) {$i_\mathrm{c}$};
            \node[siglabel, above] at (uLabelPos |- pllWestThird) {$\varepsilon$};
            \node[siglabel, above] at (uLabelPos |- pllWestBelow) {$\omega$};
            \draw[thick, ->] (motor.shaft) ++(0.4,0.24) arc[start angle = 40, end angle = -40, radius = 0.5];
            \node[right] at ($(motor.shaft tip)+(0.3,0)$) {$n,T$};
            \draw[thick, ->] (motor.west) to (pll.east);
            \draw[thick] ($(ctdcQuarterTop |- conv.north)$) to [short, -o] ++(0,0.5) coordinate (DC_link_right);
            \draw[thick] ($(ctdcQuarterLeftTop |- conv.north)$) to [short, -o] ++(0,0.5) coordinate (DC_link_left);
            \draw[thick] (DC_link_left) to [open, v^=$u_{\mathrm{DC}}$, voltage = straight] (DC_link_right);
        \end{circuitikz}
        \caption{Overview of a field-oriented control system for a PMSM drive. The phase-locked loop (PLL) is used to filter the rotor position and speed based on rotary sensors (e.g., resolver).}
        \label{fig:foc_SM_high_level}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Regular sampling and ZOH %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Regular sampling in a fully digital control design}
    \begin{columns}[c,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.54\textwidth}
            \begin{varblock}{Sample-to-sample view}
                If the machine model is discretized with zero-order held voltage input, the regular-sampling hold effect is already included in
                \begin{equation}
                    \bm{x}[k+1]=\bm{f}(\bm{x}[k],\bm{u}[k]).
                \end{equation}
                An additional consideration of the reference delay (as in continuous time) is not required in a fully digital controller.
            \end{varblock}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.43\textwidth}
            \centering
            \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm]
                \draw[->,thick] (0,0) -- (4.35,0) node[right] {$t$};
                \foreach \x/\lab in {0/$t[k]$,2/$t[k+1]$,4/$t[k+2]$}{
                        \draw[thick] (\x,0.08) -- (\x,-0.08) node[below] {\lab};
                        \draw[gray!60,densely dotted] (\x,0) -- (\x,1.75);
                    }
                \draw[signalalpha, very thick]
                (0,0.80) -- (2,0.80) -- (2,1.20) -- (4,1.20);
                \draw[dashed, gray] (1,0) -- (1,1.55) node[above] {midpoint};
                \draw[dashed, gray] (3,0) -- (3,1.55) node[above] {midpoint};
                \node at (1,0.48) {$\bm{u}^{\mathrm{appl}}[k]$};
                \node at (3,0.88) {$\bm{u}^{*}[k]$};
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
    \vspace{0.25cm}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item<2-> The integer controller-processing delay remains and must be handled explicitly.
        \item<3-> Time-critical decoupling and transformation terms should be evaluated at the effective PWM interval.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Prediction %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Single-step prediction before triggering the control loop}
    The voltage currently stored in the PWM unit is known and acts during the present pulse period:
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{u}^{\mathrm{appl}}[k] \quad \Rightarrow \quad [t[k],t[k+1]).
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Based on the machine model, a \hl{one-step prediction} can be performed to estimate the current at the time of controller output update:
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            \hat{\bm{i}}[k+1|k]={} & \left(\bm{I}-\bm{L}[k]^{-1}\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}(-\omega[k]T_\mathrm{s})T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}\right)\bm{i}[k]
            +\bm{L}[k]^{-1}(\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}(-\omega[k]T_\mathrm{s})-\bm{I})\bm{\psi}[k]                                                         \\
                                   & +\bm{L}[k]^{-1}\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}(-\omega[k]T_\mathrm{s})T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}^{\mathrm{appl}}[k] .
        \end{split}
        \label{eq:one_step_prediction_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The controller (and all model parameters required for it) is then evaluated at
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{i}}_+ = \hat{\bm{i}}[k+1|k],\qquad
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_+ = \bm{f}_{\psi_\mathrm{s}}(\hat{\bm{i}}_+),\qquad
        \hat{\bm{L}}_+ = \bm{L}(\hat{\bm{i}}_+)
    \end{equation}
    to compensate for the control delay. \pause Hence, in the following \hl{we implicitly assume that the prediction step is performed before the controller evaluation} and for sake of brevity will not explicitly write the prediction arguments in the controller equations.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsubsection{Current control}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% High-level current control structure %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{High-level current control structure}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Decouple multi-input multi-output (MIMO) dynamics by a feedforward decoupling block
        \item<2-> Design two independent single-input single-output (SISO) controllers
        \item<3-> Compensate the digital control delay by a one-step model prediction
        \item<4-> Compensate for inverter nonlinearity (not explicitly shown)
    \end{itemize}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}[node distance=1.05cm]
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sum0) {};
            \node[ctrlblock, align=center, right=1.15cm of sum0, minimum width=2.1cm, minimum height=1.1cm] (ctrl) {Feedback\\controller};
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$}, right=0.6cm of ctrl] (sum1) {};
            \node[ctrlblock, align=center, right=1.8cm of sum1, minimum width=2.05cm, minimum height=1.1cm] (inv) {Inverter\\plant};
            \node[ctrlblock, align=center, right=1.15cm of inv, minimum width=1.50cm, minimum height=1.1cm] (plant) {Machine\\plant};
            \node[ctrlblock, align=center, below=0.2cm of ctrl, minimum width=2.1cm, minimum height=1.1cm] (dec) {MIMO\\decoupling};
            \node[ctrlblock, align=center, below=2cm of sum1, minimum width=2.0cm, minimum height=1.1cm] (pred) {Model\\prediction};
            \node[right=1.3cm of plant] (out0) {};
            \coordinate (tap0) at ($(out0)!0.5!(plant.east)$);
            \node[left=1.25cm of sum0] (r0) {};
            \coordinate (predinA) at ($(pred.south east)!0.25!(pred.north east)$);
            \coordinate (predinB) at ($(pred.south east)!0.75!(pred.north east)$);
            \coordinate (predout) at (pred.west);
            \coordinate (predfbtap) at (dec.west -| sum0.south);
            \coordinate (uinv) at ($(inv.east)!0.5!(plant.west)$);
            \begin{scope}[every node/.style={font=\footnotesize}]
                \draw[->, thick] (r0) -- node[above, near start] {$\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}^{*}[k\!+\!1]$} (sum0.west);
                \draw[->, thick] (sum0.east) -- node[above] {} (ctrl.west);
                \draw[->, thick] (ctrl.east) -- node[above] {} (sum1.west);
                \draw[->, thick] (dec.east) -| (sum1.south);
                \draw[->, thick] (sum1.east) -- node[above] {$\bm{u}_\mathrm{s,dq}^{*}[k\!+\!1]$} (inv.west);
                \draw[->, thick] (inv.east) -- node[above] {$\bar{\bm{u}}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k]$} (plant.west);
                \draw[thick] (plant.east) to[short, -*] (tap0.center);
                \draw[->, thick] (plant.east) -- node[above] {$\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k]$} (out0.center);
                \draw[->, thick] (tap0.center) to[short, *-] node[pos=0.32, right] {} (tap0.center |- predinA) -- (predinA);
                \draw[->, thick] (uinv) to [short, *-] node[pos=0.32, left] {} (uinv |-  predinB) -- (predinB);
                \draw[->, thick] (pred.west) -|  node[pos=0.24, below] {$\hat{\bm{i}}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k\!+\!1|k]$} (sum0.south);
                \draw[->, thick] (predfbtap) to [short, *-] (dec.west);
            \end{scope}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{MIMO current loop with one-step model prediction for compensation of the digital control delay}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Target dynamics %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Target dynamics after decoupling}
    Consider as a starting point the discrete-time stator current equation from \eqref{eq:current_diff_eq_RK1_alpha_beta}:
    \begin{equation*}
        \bm{i}[k+1]=\left(\bm{I}-\bm{L}^{-1}[k]\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}\right)\bm{i}[k]
        +\bm{L}^{-1}[k](\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]-\bm{I})\bm{\psi}[k]
        +\bm{L}^{-1}[k]\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}[k]
    \end{equation*}
    with \hl{short notation} $\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k] = \bm{T}_\mathrm{p}(-\omega[k]T_\mathrm{s})$ for brevity. \pause We are searching for a \hl{feedforward decoupling structure} that results in a desired diagonal current model of the form
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{i}[k+1]=\left(\bm{I}-\bm{D}^{-1}[k]T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}\right)\bm{i}[k]+\bm{D}^{-1}[k]T_\mathrm{s}\bm{v}[k],
        \label{eq:target_diag_model_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    with a \hl{desired diagonal inductance matrix}
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{D}[k]=\operatorname{diag}\left(L_{\mathrm{dd}}[k],L_{\mathrm{qq}}[k]\right),
    \end{equation}\pause%
    and a \hl{new input} $\bm{v}[k]$ resulting in the following decoupled first-order current dynamics:
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            i_\mathrm{s,d}[k+1] & =\left(1-\frac{T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}}{L_{\mathrm{dd}}[k]}\right)i_\mathrm{s,d}[k]+\frac{T_\mathrm{s}}{L_{\mathrm{dd}}[k]}v_\mathrm{d}[k], \\
            i_\mathrm{s,q}[k+1] & =\left(1-\frac{T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}}{L_{\mathrm{qq}}[k]}\right)i_\mathrm{s,q}[k]+\frac{T_\mathrm{s}}{L_{\mathrm{qq}}[k]}v_\mathrm{q}[k].
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Decoupling law %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Discrete-time MIMO decoupling}
    Write \eqref{eq:current_diff_eq_RK1_alpha_beta} as
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{i}[k+1]=\bm{A}[k]\bm{i}[k]+\bm{B}[k]\bm{u}[k]+\bm{e}[k],
    \end{equation}\pause%
    with
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{A}[k]=\bm{I}-\bm{L}^{-1}[k]\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s},\quad
        \bm{e}[k]=\bm{L}^{-1}[k](\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]-\bm{I})\bm{\psi}[k],\quad
        \bm{B}[k]=\bm{L}^{-1}[k]\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}[k]T_\mathrm{s}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Define the \hl{input transformation} as
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{u}[k]=\bm{u}_{\psi}[k]+\bm{F}[k]\bm{i}[k]+\bm{P}[k]\bm{v}[k]
    \end{equation}
    with the \hl{new controller action} $\bm{v}[k]$ and the \hl{decoupling terms} $\bm{u}_{\psi}[k]$, $\bm{F}[k]$ and $\bm{P}[k]$ to be determined. \pause Matching \eqref{eq:target_diag_model_addendum} gives
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{e}[k]+\bm{B}[k]\bm{u}_{\psi}[k]=\bm{0},\quad
        \bm{A}[k]+\bm{B}[k]\bm{F}[k]=\bm{I}-\bm{D}^{-1}[k]T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s},
    \end{equation}
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{B}[k]\bm{P}[k]=\bm{D}^{-1}[k]T_\mathrm{s} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Decoupling result %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Discrete-time MIMO decoupling (cont.)}
    Since
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{B}^{-1}[k]=\frac{1}{T_\mathrm{s}}\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]\bm{L}[k],
    \end{equation}\pause%
    the decoupling terms are
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{u}_{\psi}[k]=\frac{\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]-\bm{I}}{T_\mathrm{s}}\bm{\psi}[k],
        \quad
        \bm{P}[k]=\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]\bm{L}[k]\bm{D}^{-1}[k],
    \end{equation}
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{F}[k]=\left(\bm{I}-\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]\bm{L}[k]\bm{D}^{-1}[k]\right)R_\mathrm{s} .
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The \hl{modified voltage command} for the diagonal PT1 current dynamics in \eqref{eq:target_diag_model_addendum} is then given by
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{u}^{*}[k]=\frac{\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]-\bm{I}}{T_\mathrm{s}}\bm{\psi}[k]
        +\left(\bm{I}-\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]\bm{L}[k]\bm{D}^{-1}[k]\right)R_\mathrm{s}\bm{i}[k]
        +\bm{T}_\mathrm{p}^{-1}[k]\bm{L}[k]\bm{D}^{-1}[k]\bm{v}[k] .
        \label{eq:decoupling_law_addendum}
    \end{equation}
    Substitution of \eqref{eq:decoupling_law_addendum} into \eqref{eq:current_diff_eq_RK1_alpha_beta} yields \eqref{eq:target_diag_model_addendum}.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Resulting decoupled SISO control loops %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Resulting decoupled SISO control loops}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item<2-> \textbf{Assumption:} perfect decoupling and compensation of the digital control delay by a one-step model prediction.
        \item<3-> \textbf{Consequence:} design of two independent (but structurally identical) SISO controllers for the d- and q-axis current loops.
    \end{itemize}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{subfigure}[t]{0.49\textwidth}
            \centering
            \resizebox{0.98\linewidth}{!}{%
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=0.60cm,y=0.95cm]
                    \coordinate (r) at (-1.20,0.00);
                    \coordinate (tapr) at (0.00,0.00);
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumc) at (1.55,0.00) {};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.35cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gf) at (4.55,1.55) {$G_{\mathrm{f,d}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.35cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gc) at (4.55,0.00) {$G_{\mathrm{c,d}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}] (sumv) at (7.55,0.00) {};
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}] (sumd) at (9.85,0.00) {};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.18cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gp) at (12.25,0.00) {$G_{\mathrm{p,d}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \coordinate (tapy) at ($(gp.east)+(0.61,0)$);
                    \coordinate (yout) at ($(tapy)+(0.95,0)$);
                    \coordinate (dist) at ($(sumd.center)+(0,1.20)$);
                    \begin{scope}[every node/.style={font=\footnotesize}]
                        \draw[thick] (r) -- node[above, near start] {$i_{\mathrm{s,d}}^{*}$} (tapr);
                        \draw[thick, ->] (tapr) to[short, *-] (sumc.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (tapr) |- node[pos=0.34, left] {} (gf.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumc.east) -- node[above] {$e_\mathrm{d}$} (gc.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (gc.east) -- node[above] {$v_{\mathrm{c,d}}$} (sumv.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (gf.east) -| node[pos=0.18, above] {$v_{\mathrm{f,d}}$} (sumv.north);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumv.east) -- node[above] {$v_\mathrm{d}$} (sumd.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (dist) -- node[right, near start] {$d_\mathrm{d}$} (sumd.north);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumd.east) -- node[above] {} (gp.west);
                        \draw[thick] (gp.east) to[short, -*] (tapy);
                        \draw[->, thick] (tapy) -- node[above] {$i_{\mathrm{s,d}}$} (yout);
                        \draw[->, thick] (tapy) |- ++(0,-1.08) -| (sumc.south);
                    \end{scope}
                \end{tikzpicture}%
            }
            \caption{Equivalent decoupled d-axis current loop.}
        \end{subfigure}
        \hfill
        \begin{subfigure}[t]{0.49\textwidth}
            \centering
            \resizebox{0.98\linewidth}{!}{%
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=0.60cm,y=0.95cm]
                    \coordinate (r) at (-1.20,0.00);
                    \coordinate (tapr) at (0.00,0.00);
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumc) at (1.55,0.00) {};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.35cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gf) at (4.55,1.55) {$G_{\mathrm{f,q}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.35cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gc) at (4.55,0.00) {$G_{\mathrm{c,q}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}] (sumv) at (7.55,0.00) {};
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}] (sumd) at (9.85,0.00) {};
                    \node[ctrlblock, align=center, font=\footnotesize, minimum width=1.18cm, minimum height=0.68cm] (gp) at (12.25,0.00) {$G_{\mathrm{p,q}}(\mathrm{z})$};
                    \coordinate (tapy) at ($(gp.east)+(0.61,0)$);

                        \draw[->, thick] (tapr) |- node[pos=0.34, left] {} (gf.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumc.east) -- node[above] {$e_\mathrm{q}$} (gc.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (gc.east) -- node[above] {$v_{\mathrm{c,q}}$} (sumv.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (gf.east) -| node[pos=0.18, above] {$v_{\mathrm{f,q}}$} (sumv.north);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumv.east) -- node[above] {$v_\mathrm{q}$} (sumd.west);
                        \draw[->, thick] (dist) -- node[right, near start] {$d_\mathrm{q}$} (sumd.north);
                        \draw[->, thick] (sumd.east) -- node[above] {} (gp.west);
                        \draw[thick] (gp.east) to[short, -*] (tapy);
                        \draw[->, thick] (tapy) -- node[above] {$i_{\mathrm{s,q}}$} (yout);
                        \draw[->, thick] (tapy) |- ++(0,-1.08) -| (sumc.south);
                    \end{scope}
                \end{tikzpicture}%
            }
            \caption{Equivalent decoupled q-axis current loop.}
        \end{subfigure}
        \caption{Equivalent SISO current-control loops obtained after MIMO decoupling considering closed-loop controllers $G_\mathrm{c}$, reference prefilters $G_\mathrm{f}$, and external disturbances $d$ acting on the plant systems $G_\mathrm{p}$ (sampling time indices $k$ are dropped for brevity).}
        \label{fig:SISO_current_control_loops_FOC_SM}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% SISO plant %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Resulting SISO current plants}
    For one axis $\nu\in\{\mathrm{d},\mathrm{q}\}$ the current dynamics yield (also considering an input disturbance $d_\nu$)
    \begin{equation}
        i_\nu[k+1]=a_\nu[k] i_\nu[k]+b_\nu[k]\left(v_\nu[k] + d_\nu[k]\right),
        \label{eq:siso_current_plant_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    with
    \begin{equation}
        a_\mathrm{d}[k]=1-\frac{T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}}{L_\mathrm{dd}[k]},\quad
        b_\mathrm{d}[k]=\frac{T_\mathrm{s}}{L_\mathrm{dd}[k]},\qquad
        a_\mathrm{q}[k]=1-\frac{T_\mathrm{s}R_\mathrm{s}}{L_\mathrm{qq}[k]},\quad
        b_\mathrm{q}[k]=\frac{T_\mathrm{s}}{L_\mathrm{qq}[k]}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The \hl{plant transfer function} for the current controller at the sampling instant $k$ is given by
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},\nu}(\mathrm{z})=\frac{I_\nu(\mathrm{z})}{V_\nu(\mathrm{z})}=\frac{b_\nu[k]}{\mathrm{z}-a_\nu[k]}.
        \label{eq:siso_plant_tf_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Parameters are evaluated at the actual operating point or frozen at nominal values. \pause%
        \item Formally, the plant is linear quasi-parameter-varying (qLPV) due to magnetic saturation. Hence, \eqref{eq:siso_plant_tf_addendum} is an (adaptive) linear approximation of the actual nonlinear plant. \pause%
        \item For sake of brevity, we will drop the time index $k$ dependency of the transfer functions in the following.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% PI controller %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Discrete-time current controller with prefilter path}
    From the beginning, the controller action is decomposed into a \hl{PI feedback controller} path and a parallel \hl{prefilter} path:
    \begin{equation}
        e_\nu[k]=i_\nu^{*}[k]-i_\nu[k],
        \qquad
        v_\nu[k]=v_{\mathrm{c},\nu}[k]+v_{\mathrm{f},\nu}[k].
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Utilizing a simple explicit Euler integration for the integral part, we have the following control actions:
    \begin{alignat}{3}
         & \text{Integral state update}: \quad      & x_{\mathrm{I},\nu}[k] & =x_{\mathrm{I},\nu}[k-1]+T_\mathrm{s}e_\nu[k],                             \\
         & \text{PI feedback control output}: \quad & v_{\mathrm{c},\nu}[k] & =K_{\mathrm{p},\nu}[k]e_\nu[k]+K_{\mathrm{i},\nu}[k]x_{\mathrm{I},\nu}[k], \\
         & \text{Prefilter output}: \quad           & v_{\mathrm{f},\nu}[k] & =K_{\mathrm{f},\nu}[k]i_\nu^{*}[k].
    \end{alignat}\pause%
    Here, $K_{\mathrm{p},\nu}$, $K_{\mathrm{i},\nu}$, and $K_{\mathrm{f},\nu}$ are the \hl{proportional, integral, and prefilter gains}, respectively. \pause To react on changing plant parameters, the controller gains are also considered as varying. The resulting \hl{controller / prefilter transfer functions} are then given by,
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{c},\nu}(\mathrm{z})=K_{\mathrm{p},\nu}[k]+\frac{K_{\mathrm{i},\nu}[k]T_\mathrm{s}\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-1},
        \qquad
        G_{\mathrm{f},\nu}(\mathrm{z})=K_{\mathrm{f},\nu}[k].
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Closed loop transfer functions %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Closed-loop transfer functions}
    For the SISO control loops from \figref{fig:SISO_current_control_loops_FOC_SM}, the \hl{closed-loop transfer functions} from the reference input $I^{*}(\mathrm{z})$ and the disturbance input $D(\mathrm{z})$ to the output current $I(\mathrm{z})$ are given by\footnote{For readability, we omit the axis index $\nu$ and time index $k$ representing varying plant behavior.}
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{I(\mathrm{z})}{I^{*}(\mathrm{z})}=T_\mathrm{r}(z)=\frac{G_{\mathrm{p}}(\mathrm{z})\left(G_{\mathrm{c}}(\mathrm{z})+G_{\mathrm{f}}(\mathrm{z})\right)}{1+G_{\mathrm{p}}(\mathrm{z})G_{\mathrm{c}}(\mathrm{z})},
        \qquad
        \frac{I(\mathrm{z})}{D(\mathrm{z})}=T_\mathrm{d}(z)=\frac{G_{\mathrm{p}}(\mathrm{z})}{1+G_{\mathrm{p}}(\mathrm{z})G_{\mathrm{c}}(\mathrm{z})}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Considering the previous specified transfer functions for the plant, controller, and prefilter,
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p}}(\mathrm{z})=\frac{b}{\mathrm{z}-a},
        \qquad
        G_{\mathrm{c}}(\mathrm{z})=K_\mathrm{p}+\frac{K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-1},
        \qquad
        G_{\mathrm{f}}(\mathrm{z})=K_\mathrm{f},
    \end{equation}\pause%
    one obtains
    \begin{equation}
        T_\mathrm{r}(z)=\frac{b\left[(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s})\mathrm{z}-(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f})\right]}{\Delta(\mathrm{z})},
        \quad
        T_\mathrm{d}(z)=\frac{b(\mathrm{z}-1)}{\Delta(\mathrm{z})}.
        \label{eq:closed_loop_transfer_functions_current_control_FOC_SM}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    with the \hl{closed-loop characteristic polynomial}
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta(\mathrm{z})=\mathrm{z}^2+\left[b\left(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}\right)-(1+a)\right]\mathrm{z}+a-bK_\mathrm{p}.
        \label{eq:closed_loop_den_addendum}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Closed-loop poles %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Closed-loop poles}
    The \hl{closed-loop poles} are the roots of \eqref{eq:closed_loop_den_addendum}:
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{1,2}=\frac{1+a-b\left(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}\right)\pm
            \sqrt{\left[b\left(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}\right)-(1+a)\right]^2-4\left(a-bK_\mathrm{p}\right)}}{2}.
        \label{eq:poles_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Choose \hl{desired poles} $\lambda_1$ and $\lambda_2$ with
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta_\mathrm{des}(\mathrm{z})=(\mathrm{z}-\lambda_1)(\mathrm{z}-\lambda_2)
        =\mathrm{z}^2-S_\lambda\mathrm{z}+P_\lambda,
    \end{equation}\pause%
    where
    \begin{equation}
        S_\lambda=\lambda_1+\lambda_2,
        \qquad
        P_\lambda=\lambda_1\lambda_2.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Matching coefficients in \eqref{eq:closed_loop_den_addendum} gives
    \begin{equation}
        K_\mathrm{p}=\frac{a-P_\lambda}{b},
        \qquad
        K_\mathrm{i}=\frac{1-S_\lambda+P_\lambda}{bT_\mathrm{s}}.
        \label{eq:pole_placement_gains_addendum}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Damping and rho %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Design choice via damping and transient factor}
    To analyze the impact of the pole location $\lambda_{1,2}$ on the transient response, we represent the poles as a \hl{complex-conjugate pair}
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{1,2}=r\mathrm{e}^{\pm \mathrm{j}\theta},
        \qquad 0<r<1.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Here, $r$ is the magnitude of the poles (constrained to ensure stability) and $\theta$ is the angle. \pause Introduce a logarithmic \hl{transient factor}
    \begin{equation}
        \rho=-\ln(r),\qquad r=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    With this we can express the \hl{damping} relation as
    \begin{equation}
        d=\frac{\rho}{\sqrt{\rho^2+\theta^2}}
        \quad \Rightarrow \quad
        \theta=\kappa\rho,
        \qquad
        \kappa=\frac{\sqrt{1-d^2}}{d},
    \end{equation}\pause%
    and define the pole location as a function of the design parameters $\rho$ and $d$:
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{1,2}=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}\mathrm{e}^{\pm \mathrm{j}\kappa\rho} = \mathrm{e}^{-\rho}\mathrm{e}^{\pm \mathrm{j}\frac{\sqrt{1-d^2}}{d}\rho}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% rho and settling time %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Relation between $\rho$ and settling time}
    Considering the idealized second-order closed-loop system, the \hl{free transient response} contains the envelope
    \begin{equation}
        |i_\mathrm{h}[k]|\propto r^k=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho k}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    By design a relative envelope (settling corridor) $\varepsilon$ is reached after $N_\varepsilon$ samples:
    \begin{equation}
        \mathrm{e}^{-\rho N_\varepsilon}=\varepsilon.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence, we can directly relate the transient factor $\rho$ to the \hl{settling time} in samples $N_\varepsilon$ or vice versa calculate the number of samples until a certain settling corridor $\varepsilon$ is reached:
    \begin{equation}
        \rho=\frac{\ln(1/\varepsilon)}{N_\varepsilon}, \qquad N_\varepsilon=\frac{\ln(1/\varepsilon)}{\rho}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Example cases:
    \begin{equation}
        N_{5\%}\approx\frac{3.00}{\rho},
        \qquad
        N_{2\%}\approx\frac{3.91}{\rho}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The settling time (in seconds) is then $t_\varepsilon\approx N_\varepsilon T_\mathrm{s}$.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Controller gains with d and rho %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Controller parameters from $d$ and $\rho$}
    With
    \begin{equation}
        S_\lambda=2\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}\cos(\kappa\rho),
        \qquad
        P_\lambda=\mathrm{e}^{-2\rho},
    \end{equation}
    insert $S_\lambda$ and $P_\lambda$ into \eqref{eq:pole_placement_gains_addendum}. \pause From this we can directly derive the controller gains as a function of the design parameters $d$ and $\rho$:
    \begin{equation}
        K_\mathrm{p}(d,\rho)=\frac{a-\mathrm{e}^{-2\rho}}{b}, \quad K_\mathrm{i}(d,\rho)=\frac{1-2\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}\cos(\kappa\rho)+\mathrm{e}^{-2\rho}}{bT_\mathrm{s}}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Some interpretation remarks:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textbf{Damping}: $d\in[0,1]$: defines the transient response shape (underdamped / oscillatory up to critically damped for $d\rightarrow 1$). We do not consider $d>1$ (overdamped) since it results in a slow response.\pause%
        \item \textbf{Transient factor}: $\rho>0$: defines the transient response speed (settling time). The larger $\rho$, the faster the response. However, very large $\rho$ can lead to high controller gains and thus noise sensitivity and potential inverter saturation.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Pole location based on $d$ and $\rho$ %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Pole location based $d$ and $\rho$}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering

\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Pre-filter impact and design %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Pre-filter impact and design}
    From \eqref{eq:closed_loop_transfer_functions_current_control_FOC_SM} one can observe that the prefilter gain $K_\mathrm{f}$ only impacts the reference tracking transfer function but not the disturbance transfer function. Particularly it shapes the \hl{reference transfer function's zero}:
    \begin{gather}
        \frac{I(\mathrm{z})}{I^{*}(\mathrm{z})}=\frac{b(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s})(\mathrm{z}-z_\mathrm{r})}{\Delta(\mathrm{z})},\\
        z_\mathrm{r}=\frac{K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f}}{K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}},
        \qquad
        K_\mathrm{f}=\frac{z_\mathrm{r}K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}}{1-z_\mathrm{r}}-K_\mathrm{p}.
    \end{gather}\pause%
    \vspace{-0.15cm}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item $z_\mathrm{r}\rightarrow 1$: large effective prefilter action, fast initial rise, typically larger overshoot.\pause%
        \item $z_\mathrm{r}=0$: conservative choice, smaller overshoot, slower rise.\pause%
        \item $z_\mathrm{r}<0$: rarely useful; it may introduce alternating sample-to-sample behavior.\pause%
    \end{itemize}
    \vspace{-0.3cm}
    \begin{varblock}{Recommended default choices}
        \small
        \begin{itemize}
            \item $d=1$: choose $z_\mathrm{r}=\lambda=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}$ to cancel one repeated pole in the nominal reference path.\pause%
            \item $0<d<1$: choose $z_\mathrm{r}=\Re\{\lambda_1\}=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}\cos(\kappa\rho)$ as a balanced default.
        \end{itemize}
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Impact of the reference prefilter for $d=0.9$ and $\rho=0.35$ %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Impact of the reference prefilter for $d=0.9$ and $\rho=0.35$}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{axis}[
                    width=0.84\textwidth,
                    height=0.55\textheight,
                    xmin=0, xmax=16,
                    ymin=0, ymax=1.25,
                    xtick={0,5,10,15},
                    ytick={0,0.5,1.0},
                    grid=both,
                    minor tick num=1,
                    tick label style={font=\small},
                    label style={font=\small},
                    legend style={draw=none, font=\small, at={(0.5,1.03)}, anchor=south, legend columns=2},
                    xlabel={sample $k$},
                    ylabel={$i[k]/i^{*}$},
                    scale only axis
                ]

                % Starting point of the evaluation: chosen d and rho.
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{0.9}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{0.35}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\kappavalue}{sqrt(1-\dvalue^2)/\dvalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rvalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\thetavalue}{\kappavalue*\rhovalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\zrfilt}{\rvalue*cos(deg(\thetavalue))}
                % Standard PI case (without prefilter) for the same example setting.
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\zrstd}{(0.999-\rvalue^2)/(1+0.999-2*\rvalue*cos(deg(\thetavalue)))}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\qfilt}{(\rvalue^2+\zrfilt-\rvalue*(1+\zrfilt)*cos(deg(\thetavalue)))/(\rvalue*(1-\zrfilt)*sin(deg(\thetavalue)))}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\qstd}{(\rvalue^2+\zrstd-\rvalue*(1+\zrstd)*cos(deg(\thetavalue)))/(\rvalue*(1-\zrstd)*sin(deg(\thetavalue)))}

                \def\coordlistfilt{(0,0)}
                \def\coordliststd{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yfilt}{1 - (\rvalue)^(\k)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*\k)) + \qfilt*(\rvalue)^(\k)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*\k))}
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\ystd}{1 - (\rvalue)^(\k)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*\k)) + \qstd*(\rvalue)^(\k)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*\k))}
                        \xdef\coordlistfilt{\coordlistfilt (\k,\yfilt)}
                        \xdef\coordliststd{\coordliststd (\k,\ystd)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yfilthold}{1 - (\rvalue)^(15)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*15)) + \qfilt*(\rvalue)^(15)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*15))}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\ystdhold}{1 - (\rvalue)^(15)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*15)) + \qstd*(\rvalue)^(15)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*15))}
                \xdef\coordlistfilt{\coordlistfilt (16,\yfilthold)}
                \xdef\coordliststd{\coordliststd (16,\ystdhold)}

                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlistfilt};
                \addlegendentry{default prefilter}

                \addplot[black, dashed, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordliststd};
                \addlegendentry{standard PI without prefilter}

                \addplot[black!50, dotted, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};
            \end{axis}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Comparison of the reference step response of the closed-loop controller w/wo prefilter}
        \label{fig:pre_filter_impact_FOC_current_control}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Designed closed-loop transfer functions %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Designed closed-loop transfer functions}
    Starting from the previous derivations, insert the pole placement and prefilter design:
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta(z)=(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2),\qquad
        b(K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{f}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s})
        =\frac{(1-\lambda_1)(1-\lambda_2)}{1-z_\mathrm{r}} .
        \label{eq:tf_design_insert}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The designed reference transfer function becomes
    \begin{equation}
        T_\mathrm{r}(z)
        =\frac{I(z)}{I^{*}(z)}
        =
        \frac{(1-\lambda_1)(1-\lambda_2)}{1-z_\mathrm{r}}
        \frac{z-z_\mathrm{r}}{(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2)} .
        \label{eq:designed_reference_tf}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The designed input-disturbance transfer function is
    \begin{equation}
        T_\mathrm{d}(z)
        =\frac{I(z)}{U_\mathrm{d}(z)}
        =\frac{b(z-1)}{(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2)} .
        \label{eq:designed_disturbance_tf}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    With $\bar U_\mathrm{d}(z)=bU_\mathrm{d}(z)$, the normalized disturbance transfer function follows as
    \begin{equation}
        \bar T_\mathrm{d}(z)
        =\frac{I(z)}{\bar U_\mathrm{d}(z)}
        =\frac{z-1}{(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2)} .
        \label{eq:normalized_disturbance_tf}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Thus, $T_\mathrm{r}(z)$ and $\bar T_\mathrm{d}(z)$ are plant-parameter independent after the design substitution.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Reference step response %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Reference step response}
    For a unit reference step,
    \begin{equation}
        I(z)=T_\mathrm{r}(z)\frac{z}{z-1}.
        \label{eq:reference_step_z}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    For $d=1$, the default prefilter choice yields $z_\mathrm{r}=\lambda=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}$ and cancels one repeated pole:
    \begin{equation}
        T_\mathrm{r}(z)=\frac{1-\lambda}{z-\lambda}.
        \label{eq:reference_tf_d1}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence with starting current $i[0]=0$,
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{i[k]}{i^{*}}
        =1-\lambda^k
        =1-\mathrm{e}^{-\rho k},
        \qquad k=0,1,2,\ldots .
        \label{eq:reference_sequence_d1}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    For $0<d<1$, define
    \begin{equation}
        r=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho},\qquad
        \theta=\kappa\rho,\qquad
        \kappa=\frac{\sqrt{1-d^2}}{d},\qquad
        z_\mathrm{r}=r\cos(\theta).
        \label{eq:pole_params_complex}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The exact sequence is
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{i[k]}{i^{*}}
        =1-r^k\cos(k\theta)
        +\frac{r\sin(\theta)}{1-r\cos(\theta)}\,r^k\sin(k\theta).
        \label{eq:reference_sequence_complex}
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Disturbance step response %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Disturbance step response}
    For a unit input-voltage disturbance step,
    \begin{equation}
        U_\mathrm{d}(z)=\frac{z}{z-1},
        \qquad
        I(z)=T_\mathrm{d}(z)U_\mathrm{d}(z)
        =\frac{bz}{(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2)} .
        \label{eq:disturbance_step_z}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    For $d=1$, with $\lambda=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}$ and starting current $i[0]=0$,
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{z}{(z-\lambda)^2}
        \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
        \frac{i[k]}{b}
        =k\lambda^{k-1}
        =k\,\mathrm{e}^{-\rho(k-1)},\qquad k\ge 1.
        \label{eq:disturbance_sequence_d1}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    For $0<d<1$, with $\lambda_{1,2}=r\mathrm{e}^{\pm\mathrm{j}\theta}$,
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{z}{(z-\lambda_1)(z-\lambda_2)}
        \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
        \frac{i[k]}{b}
        =
        r^{k-1}\frac{\sin(k\theta)}{\sin(\theta)},
        \qquad k\ge 0 .
        \label{eq:disturbance_sequence_complex}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence, the disturbance-response shape is determined only by the designed poles; the plant parameter $b$ only remains as physical voltage-to-current scaling.
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Idealized reference step-response based on $d$ and $\rho$ %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Idealized reference step-responses (with recommended prefilter design)}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{groupplot}[
                    group style={group size=3 by 3, horizontal sep=0.56cm, vertical sep=0.62cm,
                            x descriptions at=edge bottom, y descriptions at=edge left},
                    width=0.280\textwidth,
                    height=0.19\textheight,
                    xlabel={sample $k$},
                    xmin=0, xmax=16,
                    ymin=0, ymax=1.50,
                    xtick={0,5,10,15},
                    ytick={0,0.5,1.0,1.5},
                    grid=both,
                    minor tick num=1,
                    tick label style={font=\scriptsize},
                    label style={font=\scriptsize},
                    scale only axis
                ]

                % -----------------------------------------------------------------
                % Analytical time-series solution used in every panel
                % -----------------------------------------------------------------
                % For d = 1:
                %   lambda = exp(-rho), z_r = lambda,
                %   y[k] = i[k]/i^* = 1 - lambda^k = 1 - exp(-rho*k).
                %
                % For 0 < d < 1:
                %   kappa = sqrt(1-d^2)/d,
                %   r     = exp(-rho),
                %   theta = kappa*rho,
                %   q     = r*sin(theta)/(1-r*cos(theta)),
                %   y[k]  = i[k]/i^*
                %         = 1 - r^k cos(k*theta) + q r^k sin(k*theta).
                %
                % Causal staircase convention:
                %   - force y[0] = 0,
                %   - evaluate the analytical expression for k = 1,...,15,
                %   - append one additional point at k = 16 to hold the last sample,
                %   - use const plot mark left such that the first jump occurs at k = 1.

                % d = 1, rho = 0.25
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{1.0}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{0.25}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\lambdavalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \def\coordlist{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvalue}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(\k)}
                        \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (\k,\yvalue)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvaluehold}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(15)}
                \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (16,\yvaluehold)}
                \nextgroupplot
                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlist};
                \addplot[black!50, dashed, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};

                % d = 1, rho = 0.5
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{1.0}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{0.5}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\lambdavalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \def\coordlist{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvalue}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(\k)}
                        \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (\k,\yvalue)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvaluehold}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(15)}
                \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (16,\yvaluehold)}
                \nextgroupplot
                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlist};
                \addplot[black!50, dashed, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};

                % d = 1, rho = 1
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{1.0}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{1.0}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\lambdavalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \def\coordlist{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvalue}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(\k)}
                        \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (\k,\yvalue)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvaluehold}{1 - (\lambdavalue)^(15)}
                \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (16,\yvaluehold)}
                \nextgroupplot
                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlist};
                \addplot[black!50, dashed, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};

                % d = 0.9, rho = 0.25
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{0.9}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{0.25}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\kappavalue}{sqrt(1-\dvalue^2)/\dvalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rvalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\thetavalue}{\kappavalue*\rhovalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\qvalue}{\rvalue*sin(deg(\thetavalue))/(1-\rvalue*cos(deg(\thetavalue)))}
                \def\coordlist{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvalue}{1 - (\rvalue)^(\k)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*\k)) + \qvalue*(\rvalue)^(\k)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*\k))}
                        \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (\k,\yvalue)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvaluehold}{1 - (\rvalue)^(15)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*15)) + \qvalue*(\rvalue)^(15)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*15))}
                \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (16,\yvaluehold)}
                \nextgroupplot
                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlist};
                \addplot[black!50, dashed, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};

                % d = 0.9, rho = 0.5
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\dvalue}{0.9}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rhovalue}{0.5}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\kappavalue}{sqrt(1-\dvalue^2)/\dvalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\rvalue}{exp(-\rhovalue)}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\thetavalue}{\kappavalue*\rhovalue}
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\qvalue}{\rvalue*sin(deg(\thetavalue))/(1-\rvalue*cos(deg(\thetavalue)))}
                \def\coordlist{(0,0)}
                \foreach \k in {1,...,15} {
                        \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvalue}{1 - (\rvalue)^(\k)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*\k)) + \qvalue*(\rvalue)^(\k)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*\k))}
                        \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (\k,\yvalue)}
                    }
                \pgfmathsetmacro{\yvaluehold}{1 - (\rvalue)^(15)*cos(deg(\thetavalue*15)) + \qvalue*(\rvalue)^(15)*sin(deg(\thetavalue*15))}
                \xdef\coordlist{\coordlist (16,\yvaluehold)}
                \nextgroupplot
                \addplot[black, very thick, const plot mark left] coordinates {\coordlist};
                \addplot[black!50, dashed, thin] coordinates {(0,1) (16,1)};

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsubsection{Anti-reset wind-up}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Integrator windup: what if the controller requests too much voltage? %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}{Integrator windup: what if the controller requests too much voltage?}
    Even if the closed-loop system is stable by design, an input constraint can drastically reduce the control performance when operating with integral feedback:\pause%
    \begin{itemize}
        \item When the control input is saturated, the integral feedback continues to integrate the control error (so-called \hl{integral/reset windup}).\pause%
        \item Typically results in large overshoots and oscillations; or in the worst case, in an unstable closed-loop system.
    \end{itemize}\pause%
    \begin{varblock}{Remark on implicit controller design assumptions}
        The previous design of the PI controller implicitly assumed that the control input can take any value (i.e., is unbounded). In practice, this is not the case due to the limited DC-link voltage and the modulation technique used. In linear control design, this issue is often addressed  via a post-hoc heuristic, the so-called \hl{anti-reset windup (ARW)} scheme, to prevent an uncontrolled runaway of the integral state.
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Motivating example: detoriated control performance due to integrator windup %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Motivating example: control performance due to integrator windup}
    \centering
    \begin{tikzpicture}
        \begin{groupplot}[
                group style={group size=2 by 2, horizontal sep=1.5cm, vertical sep=0.76cm,
                        x descriptions at=edge bottom},
                width=0.385\textwidth,
                height=0.285\textheight,
                xmin=0, xmax=10,
                grid=both,
                minor tick num=1,
                tick label style={font=\footnotesize},
                label style={font=\footnotesize},
                title style={font=\footnotesize, yshift=-0.2cm},
                scale only axis
            ]

            % Current response: d-axis
            \nextgroupplot[title={$d$-axis current}, ylabel={$i_{\mathrm{s,d}}$ / A}, ymin=-150, ymax=15]
            \addplot[signaldelta, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=id_A,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \addplot[black, dashed, thin] table[x=time_ms,y=id_ref_A,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            %add arrow pointing towards 3.5 ms / -125 A from right and label it with "increased overshoot"
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:4,-125) -- (axis cs:5,-125) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {increased overshoot};

            % Current response: q-axis
            \nextgroupplot[title={$q$-axis current}, ylabel={$i_{\mathrm{s,q}}$ / A}, ymin=-20, ymax=120]
            \addplot[signaldelta, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=iq_A,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \addplot[black, dashed, thin] table[x=time_ms,y=iq_ref_A,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:3.0, 95) -- (axis cs:4.5,75) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {increased overshoot};

            % Integrator state: d-axis
            \nextgroupplot[title={$d$-axis control action}, xlabel={time / ms}, ylabel={$u_{\mathrm{d}}$ / V}, ymin=-600, ymax=100]
            \addplot[signalalpha, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=ud_unclipped_V,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \addplot[signalalpha, dashed, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=ud_clipped_V,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:3.0, -270) -- (axis cs:4.0,-150) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {clipped voltage};
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:3.5, -500) -- (axis cs:4.5,-500) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {unclipped voltage};



            % Integrator state: q-axis
            \nextgroupplot[title={$q$-axis control action}, xlabel={time / ms}, ylabel={$u_{\mathrm{q}}$ / V}, ymin=-100, ymax=600]
            \addplot[signalalpha, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=uq_unclipped_V,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \addplot[signalalpha, dashed, very thick] table[x=time_ms,y=uq_clipped_V,col sep=comma] {fig/lec03/no_arw.csv};
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:2.5, 500) -- (axis cs:3.5,500) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {unclipped voltage};
            \draw[<-, thin] (axis cs:2.5, 300) -- (axis cs:3.5,300) node[anchor=west, font=\footnotesize, inner sep=1pt, fill=white] {clipped voltage};
        \end{groupplot}
    \end{tikzpicture}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% ARW feedback implementation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{ARW feedback implementation}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{circuitikz}[>=Latex, scale=0.8, transform shape]
            \tikzset{
                detailblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.34cm, minimum height=0.86cm, font=\small},
                intblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.10cm, minimum height=1.02cm, font=\small},
                tfblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=2.00cm, minimum height=1.90cm, inner sep=0pt},
                dublock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.72cm, minimum height=1.48cm, font=\small},
                satblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=1.64cm, minimum height=1.98cm, inner sep=0pt},
                sig/.style = {font=\small, inner sep=1.5pt},
                tap/.style = {circle, fill=black, inner sep=1.15pt}
            }
            \ctikzset{block left anchors pos=0.7, block right anchors pos=0.7}
            \def\phaseport{0.72}
            \def\smallgap{0.6cm}
            \def\medgap{1.0cm}
            \def\biggap{2.25cm}

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumd) {};
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}, below=2cm of sumd] (sumq) {};

            \coordinate[left=\smallgap of sumd] (refd);
            \coordinate[left=\smallgap of sumq] (refq);
            \draw[->, thick] (refd) -- (sumd.west);
            \draw[->, thick] (refq) -- (sumq.west);
            \node[sig, above] at ($(refd)!0.1!(sumd.west)$) {$i_\mathrm{s,d}^{*}$};
            \node[sig, above] at ($(refq)!0.1!(sumq.west)$) {$i_\mathrm{s,q}^{*}$};

            \coordinate[below=\smallgap of sumd.south] (fbd);
            \coordinate[below=\smallgap of sumq.south] (fbq);
            \draw[->, thick] (fbd) -- (fbd |- sumd.south);
            \draw[->, thick] (fbq) -- (fbq |- sumq.south);
            \node[sig, left] at ($(fbd)!0.10!(fbd |- sumd.south)$) {$i_\mathrm{s,d}$};
            \node[sig, left] at ($(fbq)!0.10!(fbq |- sumq.south)$) {$i_\mathrm{s,q}$};


            \node[detailblock, right=\medgap of sumd] (kpd) {$K_{\mathrm{p,d}}$};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of kpd] (kid);
            \node[detailblock, right=\medgap of sumq] (kpq) {$K_{\mathrm{p,q}}$};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of kpq] (kiq);

            \draw[->, thick] (sumd) -- (kpd);
            \draw[->, thick] (sumq) -- (kpq);


            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$-$}, right=1.0cm of kid] (sumid) {};
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$-$}, right=1.5cm of kiq] (sumiq) {};
            \draw[->, thick] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) to[short, *-] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) |-  (sumid.west);
            \draw[->, thick] ($(sumq.east)!0.4!(kpq.west)$) to[short, *-] ($(sumq.east)!0.4!(kpq.west)$) |-  (sumiq.west);

            \node[intblock, right=\smallgap of sumiq] (intq) {$\dfrac{\mathrm{z}T_\mathrm{s}}{\mathrm{z}-1}$};

            \node[intblock, anchor=west] (intd) at (intq.west |- sumid.center) {$\dfrac{\mathrm{z}T_\mathrm{s}}{\mathrm{z}-1}$};

            \draw[->, thick] (sumid) -- (intd);
            \draw[->, thick] (sumiq) -- (intq);

            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of intd] (kid2) {$K_{\mathrm{i,d}}$};
            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of intq] (kiq2) {$K_{\mathrm{i,q}}$};
            \draw[->, thick] (intd) -- (kid2);
            \draw[->, thick] (intq) -- (kiq2);

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$}, right=\smallgap of kid2] (sumvd) {};
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$}, right=\smallgap of kiq2] (sumvq) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (kid2) -- (sumvd);
            \draw[->, thick] (kiq2) -- (sumvq);
            \draw[->, thick] (kpd.east) -| (sumvd.south);
            \draw[->, thick] (kpq.east) -| (sumvq.south);

            \node[twoportsplitshape, circuitikz/blocks/scale=1.5, right=\medgap of $(sumvd.east)!0.5!(sumvq.east)$, t1=$\mathrm{dq}$, t2=$\mathrm{abc}$]
            (dqabc) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumvd.east) -| ($(dqabc.left up)!0.5!(sumvd.east)$) |- (dqabc.left up);
            \draw[->, thick] (sumvq.east) -| ($(dqabc.left down)!0.5!(sumvq.east)$) |- (dqabc.left down);

            \node[saturationshape, circuitikz/blocks/scale=1.5, right=\biggap of dqabc] (saturation) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right up) -- node[sig, pos=0.2, above]{$u_\mathrm{a}^*$} (saturation.left up);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right) -- node[sig, pos=0.2, above]{$u_\mathrm{b}^*$} (saturation.left);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right down) -- node[sig, pos=0.2, above]{$u_\mathrm{c}^*$} (saturation.left down);

            \draw[->, thick] (saturation.right up) -- node[sig, pos=0.7, above]{$u_\mathrm{a}$} ++(\biggap, 0);
            \draw[->, thick] (saturation.right) -- node[sig, pos=0.7, above]{$u_\mathrm{b}$} ++(\biggap, 0);
            \draw[->, thick] (saturation.right down) -- node[sig, pos=0.7, above]{$u_\mathrm{c}$} ++(\biggap, 0);

            \node[twoportshape, anchor=south, circuitikz/blocks/scale=1.5, t=$\Delta u$] (delta) at ($(dqabc.west)!0.525!(saturation.east)+(0,2.25cm)$) {};
            \coordinate (deltaBottomC) at ($(delta.south west)!0.8!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaTapC) at (deltaBottomC |- dqabc.right down);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right down) -- (deltaTapC) to [short, *-] (deltaBottomC);
            \coordinate (deltaBottomB) at ($(delta.south west)!0.5!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaTapB) at (deltaBottomB |- dqabc.right);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right) -- (deltaTapB) to [short, *-] (deltaBottomB);
            \coordinate (deltaBottomA) at ($(delta.south west)!0.2!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaTapA) at (deltaBottomA |- dqabc.right up);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.right up) -- (deltaTapA) to [short, *-] (deltaBottomA);

            %define equivalent DeltaTap coordinates at the east side of the delta block for drawing the feedback lines
            \coordinate (deltaEastB) at ($(delta.north east)!0.5!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaEastA) at ($(delta.north east)!0.2!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaEastC) at ($(delta.north east)!0.8!(delta.south east)$);

            \draw[->, thick]
            let \p1 = ($(delta.east) - (deltaBottomC)$) in
            ($(saturation.right down) + (\x1, 0)$)
            to [short, *-] ($(saturation.right down) + (\x1, 0)$)
            |- (deltaEastC);
            \draw[->, thick]
            let \p1 = ($(delta.east) - (deltaBottomB)$) in
            ($(saturation.right) + (\x1, 0)$)
            to [short, *-] ($(saturation.right) + (\x1, 0)$)
            |- (deltaEastB);
            \draw[->, thick]
            let \p1 = ($(delta.east) - (deltaBottomA)$) in
            ($(saturation.right up) + (\x1, 0)$)
            to [short, *-] ($(saturation.right up) + (\x1, 0)$)
            |- (deltaEastA);

            \node[twoportsplitshape, circuitikz/blocks/scale=1.5, anchor=east, t1=$\mathrm{dq}$, t2=$\mathrm{abc}$] (abcdq) at (dqabc.east |- delta.west) {};

            \draw[->, thick] (delta.west) --  (abcdq.east);
            \draw[->, thick] (delta.left up) -- (abcdq.right up);
            \draw[->, thick] (delta.left down) -- (abcdq.right down);

            \node[detailblock] (kawd) at (kiq2 |- abcdq.left up) {$K_{\mathrm{aw,d}}$};
            \node[detailblock] (kawq)  at (kiq2 |- abcdq.left down) {$K_{\mathrm{aw,q}}$};

            \draw[->, thick] (abcdq.left up) -- (kawd);
            \draw[->, thick] (abcdq.left down) -- (kawq);
            \draw[->, thick] (kawq.west) -| (sumiq.north);
            \draw[->, thick] (kawd.west) -| (sumid.north);

            \coordinate[below=\smallgap of dqabc.south] (epsstart);
            \draw[->, thick] (epsstart) node[below, anchor=north] {$\varepsilon$} --  (dqabc.south);
            \draw[->, thick] (dqabc.north) -- (abcdq.south);
        \end{circuitikz}%
        \caption{Controller representation with ARW feedback (reference prefilter path is not depicted for sake of simplicity)}
        \label{fig:ARW_implementation}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% ARW feedback: integrator dynamics during voltage limitation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{ARW feedback: integrator dynamics during voltage limitation}
    The unlimited integral action is
    \begin{equation}
        x^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
        =
        x_{\mathrm{i}}[k-1]
        +
        T_{\mathrm{s}}e[k], \quad v^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k] = K_{\mathrm{i}}x^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k].
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The total control action $v^*[k]
        =
        K_{\mathrm{p}} e[k]
        +
        v^+_{\mathrm{Ii}}[k] + v_\mathrm{f}[k]$ is then clipped toward
    \begin{equation}
        \overline{v}[k] = \mathrm{lim}\left\{v^*[k]\right\}, \quad \Delta v[k] = v^*[k] - \overline{v}[k].
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence, the feasible voltage contribution for the PI path is
    \begin{equation}
        v_{\mathrm{lim}}[k] = \overline{v}[k] - v_\mathrm{f}[k] \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \Delta v[k] = K_{\mathrm{p}} e[k] + v^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k] - v_{\mathrm{lim}}[k].
    \end{equation}\pause%
    As the \hl{ARW measure apply a correction feedback of the integrator state}
    \begin{equation}
        x_{\mathrm{i}}[k] = x^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k] - \frac{K_{\mathrm{aw}}}{K_{\mathrm{i}}}\Delta v[k], \quad v_{\mathrm{i}}[k] = K_{\mathrm{i}}x_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
    \end{equation}\pause%
    leading to the corrected integral voltage action
    \begin{equation}
        v_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
        =
        (1-K_{\mathrm{aw}})v_{\mathrm{i}}[k-1]
        +
        \left[\left(1-K_{\mathrm{aw}}\right)K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}-K_{\mathrm{aw}}K_{\mathrm{p}}\right]e[k]
        +
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}v_{\mathrm{lim}}[k].
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% ARW tracking transfer function %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{ARW tracking transfer function}
    For the isolated ARW tracking dynamics, i.e., $e[k]=0$, the integral voltage dynamics reduce to
    \begin{equation}
        v_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
        =
        (1-K_{\mathrm{aw}})v_{\mathrm{i}}[k-1]
        +
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}v_{\mathrm{lim}}[k].
        \label{eq:arw_isolated_tracking}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence, the \hl{ARW input-output transfer function} is\footnote{This ARW plant model is severely simplified and only provides a first approximation of the relevant dynamics practically assuming the clipping would occur on the decoupled SISO $v$ level. It does not cover the actual MIMO structure, the transformations from $v$ to $u$ (and back) as well as (inverse) Park/Clarke transformations which are in the actual ARW signal path.}
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{V_{\mathrm{i}}(\mathrm{z})}{V_{\mathrm{lim}}(\mathrm{z})}
        =
        \frac{K_{\mathrm{aw}}\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-(1-K_{\mathrm{aw}})}.
        \label{eq:arw_tracking_tf}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The corresponding \hl{ARW pole} is
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}
        =
        1-K_{\mathrm{aw}}.
        \label{eq:arw_pole}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Thus, the ARW feedback defines a first-order tracking dynamics of the integral voltage
    contribution towards the feasible PI voltage contribution.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Feedback ARW design via $K_{\mathrm R}$ %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Feedback ARW design via $K_{\mathrm{r}}$}
    A common parametrization is
    \begin{equation}
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}[k]
        =
        \frac{K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}}{K_{\mathrm{p}}+K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}}
        K_{\mathrm{r}}
        \label{eq:arw_kr_definition}
    \end{equation}
    with the ARW reference gain $K_{\mathrm{r}}$. \pause Consequently, the ARW correction is added to the stored integrator state as
    \begin{equation}
        x_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
        =
        x^+_{\mathrm{i}}[k]
        -
        \frac{T_\mathrm{s}}{K_\mathrm{p}+K_\mathrm{i}T_\mathrm{s}}K_\mathrm{r}\Delta v[k].
        \label{eq:arw_kr_state_update}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    With this choice, the error contribution in the integral voltage dynamics is
    \begin{equation}
        (1-K_{\mathrm{aw}})K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}
        -
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}K_{\mathrm{p}}
        =
        K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}\left(1-K_{\mathrm{r}}\right).
        \label{eq:arw_kr_error_contribution}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Consequently,
    \begin{equation}
        K_{\mathrm{r}}=1
        \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
        (1-K_{\mathrm{aw}})K_{\mathrm{i}}T_{\mathrm{s}}
        -
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}K_{\mathrm{p}}
        =
        0.
        \label{eq:arw_kr_one}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Interpretation: $K_{\mathrm{r}}=1$ cancels the proportional error contribution during
    limitation; $K_{\mathrm{r}}<1$ gives slower unwinding; $K_{\mathrm{r}}>1$ gives faster,
    but potentially over-aggressive, unwinding.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Pole-based ARW design %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Pole-based ARW design}
    Since the ARW tracking pole is $\lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}    =
        1-K_{\mathrm{aw}}$, one may prescribe the ARW pole directly:
    \begin{equation}
        K_{\mathrm{aw}}
        =
        1-\lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}.
        \label{eq:arw_kaw_from_pole}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    For the pole-placement current controller, useful choices are
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}
        =
        z_{\mathrm{r}}
        \qquad\text{or}\qquad
        \lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}
        =
        \mathrm{e}^{-\rho}.
        \label{eq:arw_recommended_poles}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Here, the following interpretations apply:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item $\lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}=z_{\mathrm{r}}$ gives a consistent ARW tracking speed with the reference-zero design, i.e., the ARW tracking dynamics have the same discrete-time pole as the reference-zero dynamics.\pause%
        \item $\lambda_{\mathrm{aw}}=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho}$ gives a consistent ARW tracking speed with the closed-loop decay envelope, i.e., the ARW tracking dynamics have the same decay envelope as the closed-loop response.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsubsection{Operating point selection}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% High-level view on the operating point selection (OPS) task %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{High-level view on the operating point selection (OPS) task}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{tikzpicture}[>=Latex, line width=0.9pt, font=\normalsize]
            % block
            \draw[line width=1.1pt] (0,0) rectangle (8.8,3.9);
            \draw[line width=0.7pt] (0.12,0.12) rectangle (8.68,3.78);

            % block text
            \node[align=center, text width=6.9cm] at (4.4,2.0)
            {generation of optimal current references\\[1mm]
                for the entire torque-speed range};

            % left input
            \draw[->] (-2.8,1.95) -- (0,1.95);
            \node[left] at (-2.8,1.95) {$T^*$};

            % top inputs
            \draw[->] (1.7,5.0) -- (1.7,3.9);
            \node[above] at (1.7,5.0) {$i_{\mathrm{s},\max}$};

            \draw[->] (4.4,5.0) -- (4.4,3.9);
            \node[above] at (4.4,5.0) {$u_{\mathrm{s},\max}$};

            \draw[->] (7.1,5.0) -- (7.1,3.9);
            \node[above] at (7.1,5.0) {$\omega$};

            % right outputs
            \draw[->] (8.8,2.55) -- (11.0,2.55);
            \node[anchor=west] at (9.15,2.95) {$i_{\mathrm{s,d}}^*$};

            \draw[->] (8.8,1.35) -- (11.0,1.35);
            \node[anchor=west] at (9.15,1.75) {$i_{\mathrm{s,q}}^*$};
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Operating point selection (OPS): mapping torque references towards current set points considering operational constraints of the drive (for an EESM drive, additionally $i_\mathrm{f}^*$ would be emitted while considering the max. field current $i_\mathrm{f,max}$)}
        \label{fig:OPS}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating point selection: PMSM %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{OPS problem: PMSM}
    For given $(T^*,\omega,u_{\mathrm{dc}})$, the OPS computes
    \[
        i_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^* \in \mathbb{R}^2 .
    \]\pause%
    We consider the steady-state nonlinear PMSM model:
    \begin{equation*}
        \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} = f_{\psi}\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\right),
        \qquad
        \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}},\omega\right)
        =
        \bm{R}_{\mathrm{s}}\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}
        +
        \omega \bm{J} \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}},
        \label{eq:ops_pmsm_model}
    \end{equation*}
    \begin{equation*}
        T\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\right)
        =
        \frac{3}{2}p\,
        \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^\top \bm{J} \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}},
        \qquad
        \bm{J}=
        \begin{bmatrix}
            0 & -1 \\
            1 & 0
        \end{bmatrix},
        \label{eq:ops_pmsm_torque}
    \end{equation*}\pause%
    and formulate the \hl{PMSM's OPS problem} as a constrained optimization task in the current plane:
    \begin{gather}
        \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*
        \in
        \arg\min_{\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}
        J_{\mathrm{OPS}}\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}};\omega\right)
        \\[-0.5mm]
        \text{s.t.}\qquad
        T\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\right)=T^*,
        \qquad
        \|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2\le i_{\mathrm{s},\max}, \qquad  \left\|
        \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}},\omega\right)
        \right\|_2\le
        u_{\mathrm{s},\max}(u_{\mathrm{dc}},m_{\max}) . \notag
        \label{eq:ops_pmsm_problem}
    \end{gather}\pause%
    Typical choices of $J_{\mathrm{OPS}}$ are the minimization of the total power loss $P_{\mathrm{loss}}$ or the minimization of the stator current amplitude $\|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2$ as a proxy for the losses.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating point selection: EESM %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{OPS problem: EESM}
    In the EESM case we extend the optimization vector to include the field current reference:
    \[
        \bm{\xi}^*=
        \begin{bmatrix}
            (\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*)^\top & i_{\mathrm{f}}^*
        \end{bmatrix}^{\!\top}
        \in \mathbb{R}^3 .
    \]\pause%
    Also, here we consider the steady-state nonlinear EESM model:
    \begin{equation*}
        \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm E}=f_{\psi,\mathrm E}(\bm{\xi}),
        \qquad
        \bm{u}_{\mathrm E}(\bm{\xi},\omega)
        =
        \bm{R}_{\mathrm E}\bm{\xi}+\bm{J}_{\mathrm E}(\omega)\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm E},
    \end{equation*}
    \begin{equation*}
        T(\bm{\xi})
        =
        \frac{3}{2}p\,
        (\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}})^{\top} J \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} .
    \end{equation*}\pause%
    Then, the \hl{OPS problem for the EESM} can be formulated as:
    \begin{gather}
        \bm{\xi}^*
        \in
        \arg\min_{\bm{\xi}}
        J_{\mathrm{OPS}}(\bm{\xi};\omega),
        \\[-0.5mm]
        \text{s.t.}\qquad
        T(\bm{\xi})=T^*,
        \qquad
        \|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2\le i_{\mathrm{s},\max},
        \qquad
        \|\bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bm{\xi},\omega)\|_2
        \le
        u_{\mathrm{s},\max}(u_{\mathrm{dc}},m_{\max}),\notag
        \\[-0.5mm]
        i_{\mathrm f,\min}\le i_{\mathrm f}\le i_{\mathrm f,\max},
        \qquad
        |\bm{u}_{\mathrm f}(\bm{\xi},\omega)|\le u_{\mathrm f,\max}.\notag
    \end{gather}\pause%
    In contrast to the PMSM case, minimizing the stator current amplitude $\|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2$ is not a good proxy for the losses, since the field current $i_{\mathrm f}$ can be traded off against the stator currents. Hence, at least a total copper loss model should be included in $J_{\mathrm{OPS}}$ for EESM drives.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Soft-constrained OPS in flux weakening %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Soft-constrained OPS in flux weakening}
    In \hl{flux-weakening mode}, the \hl{equality constraint $T=T^*$ may become infeasible} due to
    the current and voltage limits. Hence, the torque reference constraint must be relaxed.\\ \pause%
    For the PMSM, a \hl{soft-constrained OPS problem} can be formulated as
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{aligned}
            \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*
             & \in
            \arg\min_{\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}
            \Bigl(
            J_{\mathrm{OPS}}\!\left(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}};\omega\right)
            +
            \gamma_T \bigl(T^*-T(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}})\bigr)^2
            \Bigr)
            \\
            \text{s.t.}\qquad
             & \|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2\le i_{\mathrm{s},\max},
            \qquad
            \|\bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}},\omega)\|_2
            \le
            u_{\mathrm{s},\max}(u_{\mathrm{dc}},m_{\max}) .
        \end{aligned}
        \label{eq:ops_soft_pmsm}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Analogously, for the EESM:
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{aligned}
            \bm{\xi}^*
             & \in
            \arg\min_{\bm{\xi}}
            \Bigl(
            J_{\mathrm{OPS}}(\bm{\xi};\omega)
            +
            \gamma_T \bigl(T^*-T(\bm{\xi})\bigr)^2
            \Bigr)
            \\
            \text{s.t.}\qquad
             & \|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2\le i_{\mathrm{s},\max},
            \qquad
            \|\bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bm{\xi},\omega)\|_2
            \le
            u_{\mathrm{s},\max}(u_{\mathrm{dc}},m_{\max}),
            \\
             & i_{\mathrm f,\min}\le i_{\mathrm f}\le i_{\mathrm f,\max},
            \qquad
            |\bm{u}_{\mathrm f}(\bm{\xi},\omega)|\le u_{\mathrm f,\max}.
        \end{aligned}
        \label{eq:ops_soft_eesm}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The \hl{weighting factor} $\gamma_T>0$ prioritizes torque tracking. If $T^*$ is infeasible,
    the optimizer returns the admissible operating point with minimal torque error.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\input{fig/lec03/OPC_config} % configuration for the operating range slides
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Formal definition of the OPS contours (for IPMSM example) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Formal definition of the OPS contours (for IPMSM example)}
    We define the contours in the current plane as follows:
    \vspace{-0.2cm}
    \begin{columns}[c,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.57\textwidth}
            \begin{align*}
                \mathbb{T}(\bar T)
                 & :={\{}\bm{i}\in\mathbb{R}^2\mid T(\bm{i})=\bar T{\}},                      \\
                \mathbb{I}(\bar i)
                 & :={\{}\bm{i}\in\mathbb{R}^2\mid \|\bm{i}\|_2\le \bar i{\}},                \\
                \partial\mathbb{I}(\bar i)
                 & :={\{}\bm{i}\in\mathbb{R}^2\mid \|\bm{i}\|_2=\bar i{\}},                   \\
                \mathbb{V}(\omega,\bar u)
                 & :={\{}\bm{i}\in\mathbb{R}^2\mid \|\bm{u}(\bm{i},\omega)\|_2\le \bar u{\}}, \\
                \partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\bar u)
                 & :={\{}\bm{i}\in\mathbb{R}^2\mid \|\bm{u}(\bm{i},\omega)\|_2=\bar u{\}},
            \end{align*}
        \end{column}\pause%
        \begin{column}{0.43\textwidth}
            \begin{align*}
                \mathbb{MTPC}
                 & :=
                \bigcup_{\bar T\in\mathbb{R}}
                \arg\min_{\bm{i}\in\mathbb{T}(\bar T)} \|\bm{i}\|_2, \\
                \mathbb{MTPV}
                 & :=
                \bigcup_{\bar u>0}
                \arg\max_{\bm{i}\in\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\bar u)} T(\bm{i}).
            \end{align*}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
    \begin{varblock}{Standard operationg strategies}
        The \hl{maximum torque per current (MTPC)} and the \hl{maximum torque per voltage (MTPV)} strategy are setting the boundaries of the feasible operating range of the drive in the current plane. The MTPC strategy minimizes stator copper losses in the low-speed region, while the MTPV strategy maximizes torque at the voltage limit in the high-speed region. In between, a transition between both strategies is required.
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
