%% Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: MTPC region %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: MTPC region}
    \begin{columns}
        \begin{column}{0.525\textwidth}
            \vspace{0.4cm}\\
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[opsaxis]
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalalpha,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {yvoltnorm(x,\cA)};
                    \addplot[very thick,dashed,color=signaldelta,domain=-\rA:0,samples=140] {sqrt(max(0,\rA*\rA-x*x))};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta,domain=0:1,samples=220,variable=\y] ({xmtpcnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=0:1,samples=260,variable=\y] ({xmtpvnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,black,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ytorquenorm(x,\TA)};
                    \addplot[very thick, only marks,mark=star,mark size=4,color=signalepsilon] coordinates {(\xA,\yA)};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south east] at (axis cs:0,0.98) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalalpha,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.3,0.73) {$\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,u_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.99) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                    \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.06) {$\mathbb{MTPV}$};
                    \node[black,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.5,0.46) {$\mathbb{T}(T^*)$};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=west] at (axis cs:-0.5,0.34) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i^*_{\mathrm{s}})$};
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.475\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item Proxy for loss minimization in the low-speed region: $$J_{\mathrm{OPS}}(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}})=\|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2^2.$$
                \item<2-> Advantage: no complex loss model required, only torque and current model.
                \item<3-> Visual interpretation: tangent point of the torque contour and the current circle:
                      $$
                          \partial T(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}) = \lambda \partial \mathbb{I}(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}).
                      $$
                \item<4-> Applicable below the current and voltage limits, i.e., in the low-speed region.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: field-weakening (FW) region %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: field-weakening (FW) region}
    \begin{columns}
        \begin{column}{0.525\textwidth}
            \vspace{0.4cm}\\
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[opsaxis]
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalalpha,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {yvoltnorm(x,\cB)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta,domain=0:1,samples=220,variable=\y] ({xmtpcnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=0:1,samples=260,variable=\y] ({xmtpvnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,black,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ytorquenorm(x,\TB)};
                    \addplot[very thick, only marks,mark=star,mark size=4,color=signalepsilon] coordinates {(\xB,\yB)};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south east] at (axis cs:0,0.98) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalalpha,anchor=north] at (axis cs:-0.55,0.41) {$\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\hat{u}_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.99) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                    \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.06) {$\mathbb{MTPV}$};
                    \node[black,anchor=west] at (axis cs:-0.43,0.75) {$\mathbb{T}(T^*)$};
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.475\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item Region with active voltage constraint and remaining current margin.
                \item<2-> The OPS still tracks the requested torque, but the solution can no longer stay on the MTPC locus.
                \item<3-> Visual interpretation: the admissible operating point lies on
                      $$
                          \mathbb{T}(T^*)\cap\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\hat{u}_{\mathrm{s,max}})
                      $$
                      while still satisfying $\|\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2 < i_{\mathrm{s,max}}$.
                \item<4-> Typical transition region between MTPC-dominated operation and the hard current-limited range.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: maximum current (MC) region %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: maximum current (MC) region}
    \begin{columns}
        \begin{column}{0.525\textwidth}
            \vspace{0.4cm}\\
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[opsaxis]
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalalpha,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {yvoltnorm(x,\cC)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta,domain=0:1,samples=220,variable=\y] ({xmtpcnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=0:1,samples=260,variable=\y] ({xmtpvnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,black,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ytorquenorm(x,\TC)};
                    \addplot[very thick, only marks,mark=star,mark size=4,color=signalepsilon] coordinates {(\xC,\yC)};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south east] at (axis cs:-0.2,0.95) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalalpha,anchor=north] at (axis cs:-0.55,0.52) {$\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\hat{u}_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.99) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                    \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.06) {$\mathbb{MTPV}$};
                    \node[black,anchor=west] at (axis cs:-0.425,0.72) {$\mathbb{T}(T^*)$};
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.475\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item Region where the current and voltage constraints become simultaneously active.
                \item<2-> The OPS can no longer reduce the current magnitude; the available operating point is pinned to the feasible boundary.
                \item<3-> Visual interpretation: the optimum is located at the boundary intersection
                      $$
                          \partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})\cap\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\hat{u}_{\mathrm{s,max}}).
                      $$
                \item<4-> Further speed increase reduces the achievable torque and pushes the solution toward the MTPV boundary.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: MTPV region %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Operating range of the PMSM-OPS: MTPV region}
    \begin{columns}
        \begin{column}{0.525\textwidth}
            \vspace{0.4cm}\\
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[opsaxis]
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalalpha,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {yvoltnorm(x,\cD)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta,domain=0:1,samples=220,variable=\y] ({xmtpcnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=0:1,samples=260,variable=\y] ({xmtpvnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,black,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ytorquenorm(x,\TD)};
                    \addplot[very thick, only marks,mark=star,mark size=4,color=signalepsilon] coordinates {(\xD,\yD)};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south east] at (axis cs:0,0.98) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalalpha,anchor=north] at (axis cs:-0.3,0.15) {$\partial\mathbb{V}(\omega,\hat{u}_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.99) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                    \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.75,0.06) {$\mathbb{MTPV}$};
                    \node[black,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.17,0.5) {$\mathbb{T}(T^*)$};
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.475\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item High-speed region in which the voltage boundary determines the maximum achievable torque.
                \item<2-> Current constraint is no longer relevant, voltage limit is the dominant constraint.
                \item<3-> Visual interpretation: tangent point of the torque contour and the voltage boundary:
                      $$
                          \partial T(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}) = \lambda \partial \mathbb{V}(\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}).
                      $$
                \item<4-> The MTPV locus defines the upper torque capability in deep flux weakening.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Feasible operating range of the PMSM-OPS %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Feasible operating range of the PMSM-OPS}
    \centering
    \begin{columns}
        \begin{column}{0.55\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item The feasible operating range of the drive is defined by the MTPC and MTPV loci and the current limit.
                \item<2-> The exact shape of the feasible region depends on the specific machine characteristics.
                \item<3-> Operating points outside this range are either infeasible (current / voltage limits) or suboptimal (additional copper losses for a given torque).
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.45\textwidth}
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[opsaxisgen]
                    \path[fill=lightgray]
                    (axis cs:{xmtpcnorm(0)},0)
                    \foreach \yy in {0.00,0.01,...,0.81} { -- (axis cs:{xmtpcnorm(\yy)},{\yy}) }
                    \foreach \yy in {0.81,0.80,...,0.37} { -- (axis cs:{xcurrentnorm(\yy)},{\yy}) }
                    \foreach \yy in {0.37,0.36,...,0.00} { -- (axis cs:{xmtpvnorm(\yy)},{\yy}) }
                    \foreach \yy in {0.00,-0.01,...,-0.37} { -- (axis cs:{xmtpvnorm(abs(\yy))},{\yy}) }
                    \foreach \yy in {-0.37,-0.38,...,-0.81} { -- (axis cs:{xcurrentnorm(abs(\yy))},{\yy}) }
                    \foreach \yy in {-0.81,-0.80,...,0.00} { -- (axis cs:{xmtpcnorm(abs(\yy))},{\yy}) }
                    -- cycle;
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=-1:0,samples=180] {-ycurrentnorm(x)};
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta,domain=-1:1,samples=220,variable=\y] ({xmtpcnorm(\y)},{\y});
                    \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=-1:1,samples=260,variable=\y] ({xmtpvnorm(abs(\y))},{\y});
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south] at (axis cs:-0.25,-0.90) {$\partial\mathbb{I}(i_{\mathrm{s,max}})$};
                    \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=west] at (axis cs:-0.4,0.65) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                    \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=east] at (axis cs:-0.55,0.00) {$\mathbb{MTPV}$};
                    \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=east] at (axis cs:-0.7,0.75) {$\mathbb{MC}$};
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Operating range of the PMSM-OPS in the torque-speed plane %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Operating range of the PMSM-OPS in the torque-speed plane}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{axis}[opsspeedaxis]
                % FW feasible region in the torque-speed plane.
                % It is computed from the MTPC feasibility boundary, the MC
                % current-limit boundary, and the high-speed MTPF/MTPV locus.
                \path[fill=lightgray,opacity=0.55,draw=none]
                (axis cs:\opsTSomegaMTPCzero,0)
                foreach \k in {0,...,100} { -- (axis cs:{opsTSomeganormxy(xmtpcnorm(\k*\yR/100),\k*\yR/100)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xmtpcnorm(\k*\yR/100),\k*\yR/100)}) }
                foreach \k in {1,...,100} { -- (axis cs:{opsTSomeganormxy(xcurrentnorm(\yR + \k*(\yM-\yR)/100),\yR + \k*(\yM-\yR)/100)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xcurrentnorm(\yR + \k*(\yM-\yR)/100),\yR + \k*(\yM-\yR)/100)}) }
                foreach \k in {1,...,100} { -- (axis cs:{opsTSomeganormxy(xmtpvnorm(\yM + \k*(\opsTSyEnd-\yM)/100),\yM + \k*(\opsTSyEnd-\yM)/100)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xmtpvnorm(\yM + \k*(\opsTSyEnd-\yM)/100),\yM + \k*(\opsTSyEnd-\yM)/100)}) }
                -- (axis cs:\opsTSomegaMaxPlot,0) -- cycle;

                % MTPC operation region: same color for fill and outer contour.
                \path[fill=signalbeta!22,draw=none]
                (axis cs:0,0) -- (axis cs:0,1) -- (axis cs:1,1)
                foreach \k in {100,99,...,0} { -- (axis cs:{opsTSomeganormxy(xmtpcnorm(\k*\yR/100),\k*\yR/100)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xmtpcnorm(\k*\yR/100),\k*\yR/100)}) }
                -- cycle;

                % Auxiliary construction lines.
                \addplot[densely dotted,black,domain=0:3.08,samples=2] {1};
                \addplot[densely dotted,black] coordinates {(1,0) (1,1)};

                % Computed operating-range boundaries.
                \addplot[very thick,color=signalbeta] coordinates {(0,1) (1,1)};
                \addplot[very thick,densely dashed,color=signalbeta,domain=0:\yR,samples=220,variable=\y]
                ({opsTSomeganormxy(xmtpcnorm(\y),\y)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xmtpcnorm(\y),\y)});
                \addplot[very thick,color=signaldelta,domain=\yM:\yR,samples=220,variable=\y]
                ({opsTSomeganormxy(xcurrentnorm(\y),\y)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xcurrentnorm(\y),\y)});
                \addplot[very thick,color=signalgamma,domain=\opsTSyEnd:\yM,samples=260,variable=\y]
                ({opsTSomeganormxy(xmtpvnorm(\y),\y)},{opsTStorquenormxy(xmtpvnorm(\y),\y)});

                % Characteristic points and selected operating point.
                \addplot[only marks,mark=square*,mark size=2.4,color=signalbeta] coordinates {(1,1)};
                \addplot[only marks,mark=square*,mark size=2.4,color=signalgamma] coordinates {(\opsTSomegaMTPFcut,\opsTSTorqueMTPFcut)};

                % Region labels.
                \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=west,font=\large] at (axis cs:0.20,0.18) {$\mathbb{MTPC}$};
                \node[color=signaldelta,anchor=south,font=\large] at (axis cs:1.5,0.84) {$\mathbb{MC}$};
                \node[color=gray,anchor=west,font=\large] at (axis cs:2.30,0.30) {$\mathbb{FW}$};
                \node[color=signalgamma,anchor=west,font=\large] at (axis cs:2.40,0.51) {$\mathbb{MTPF}$};

                % Nomenclature annotations following the lecture slides.
                \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=south west,font=\scriptsize] at (axis cs:1.02,1.02)
                {$(\omega_{\mathrm{nom}},T_{\mathrm{max}})$};
                \node[color=signalbeta,anchor=west,font=\small,align=left] at (axis cs:1.25,0.33)
                {$\omega_{\mathrm{feas}}^{\mathbb{MTPC}}(T^*)$};
                \node[anchor=south,font=\scriptsize] at (axis cs:2.70,1.0) {$T_{\mathrm{max}}$};
            \end{axis}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Typical speed-torque plane for an IPMSM drive with the different operating modes}
        \label{fig:speed_torque_IPMSM_operating_range}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% OPS solution methods: high-level map %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{OPS solution methods: high-level view}
    \begin{center}
        \begin{tikzpicture}[>=Latex, line width=0.8pt, font=\normalsize]
            \tikzstyle{opsrect}=[draw, rounded corners=1.5mm, minimum width=4.1cm, minimum height=1.58cm, inner sep=0pt]
            \tikzstyle{opstext}=[align=center, text width=4cm]

            \node[opsrect, fill=gray!15] (model) at (0,3.0) {};
            \node[opstext] at (model.center) {machine model\\and constraints};
            \node[opsrect] (ana) at (-5.0,1.0) {};
            \node[opstext] at (ana.center) {analytical geometry\\solution patterns};
            \node[opsrect] (nlp) at (0,1.0) {};
            \node[opstext] at (nlp.center) {numerical constrained\\optimization};
            \node[opsrect] (lut) at (5.0,1.0) {};
            \node[opstext] at (lut.center) {Look-up tables (LUTs)\\and surrogates};
            \node[opsrect, fill=gray!15] (out) at (0,-1.05) {};
            \node[opstext] at (out.center) {real-time map\\$T^*\mapsto i^*$};

            \draw[->] (model.south west) -- (ana.north east);
            \draw[->] (model.south) -- (nlp.north);
            \draw[->] (model.south east) -- (lut.north west);
            \draw[->] (ana.south east) -- (out.north west);
            \draw[->] (nlp.south) -- (out.north);
            \draw[->] (lut.south west) -- (out.north east);
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \end{center}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item<2-> \hl{Analytical methods}: exploit special structure of linear or affine machine models.
        \item<3-> \hl{Numerical optimization}: solve problem via an (embedded) numerical solver online.
        \item<4-> \hl{Pre-computation}: solve expensive problems offline and store or learn the solution map.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}




%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Analytical geometry and algebraic roots %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Analytical OPS: quadric solution pattern}
    \setlength{\abovedisplayskip}{2pt}
    \setlength{\belowdisplayskip}{2pt}
    For affine flux-linkage models at steady state, the relevant OPS loci can be written as
    implicit quadrics in the current plane (with operating conditions parameterized by $\bm{\theta}$):
    \[
        \bm{z}=\begin{bmatrix}i_{\mathrm d}&i_{\mathrm q}&1\end{bmatrix}^{\!\top},
        \qquad
        q_k(\bm{z};\bm{\theta})=\bm{z}^\top Q_k(\bm{\theta})\bm{z},
        \qquad
        \bm{\theta}=(T^*,\omega,u_{\mathrm{dc}},i_{\max},\ldots).
    \]
    \vspace{-2mm}
    \begin{center}
        \begin{tikzpicture}[>=Latex, line width=0.75pt, font=\normalsize]
            \tikzstyle{procbox}=[draw, rounded corners=1mm, minimum width=2.82cm, minimum height=1.45cm, inner sep=0pt]
            \tikzstyle{proctext}=[align=center, text width=2.55cm]
            \node[procbox] (loci) at (0,0) {};
            \node[proctext] at (loci.center) {form active\\loci\\$q_k(\bm{z};\bm{\theta})=0$};
            \node[procbox] (poly) at (3.15,0) {};
            \node[proctext] at (poly.center) {eliminate\\variables\\$p(\bm{\eta};\bm{\theta})=0$};
            \node[procbox] (roots) at (6.30,0) {};
            \node[proctext] at (roots.center) {roots of $p=0$\\in closed form};
            \node[procbox] (select) at (9.45,0) {};
            \node[proctext] at (select.center) {select feasible\\OPS branch};
            \draw[->] (loci.east) -- (poly.west);
            \draw[->] (poly.east) -- (roots.west);
            \draw[->] (roots.east) -- (select.west);
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \end{center}
    \vspace{-2mm}\pause%
    Typical quadrics are:
    \[
        \underbrace{q_T=0}_{\text{torque hyperbola}},\qquad
        \underbrace{q_I\le 0}_{\text{current circle}},\qquad
        \underbrace{q_U\le 0}_{\text{voltage ellipse}}.
    \]
    \vspace{-2mm}\pause%
    \begin{itemize}
        \item MTPC: smallest current circle tangent to a torque hyperbola.
        \item FW: intersection of torque hyperbola and voltage ellipse.
        \item MC / MTPV: active-set intersections or tangency conditions with current/voltage limits.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Analytical geometry and algebraic roots: MTPC example %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Analytical OPS: linear IPMSM MTPC example}
    With constant inductances and $\Delta L=L_{\mathrm dd}-L_{\mathrm qq}$:
    \[
        \tau=\frac{T^*}{\frac{3}{2}p}
        =\left(\psi_{\mathrm{pm}}+\Delta L i_{\mathrm{s,d}}\right)i_{\mathrm{s,q}},
        \qquad
        \min\; i_{\mathrm{s,d}}^2+i_{\mathrm{s,q}}^2 .
    \]\pause%
    Torque and current circle as quadrics with
    $\bm{z}=[i_{\mathrm{s,d}}\ i_{\mathrm{s,q}}\ 1]^\top$:
    \[
        q_T=\bm{z}^\top
        \begin{bmatrix}
            0                  & \frac{\Delta L}{2}           & 0                            \\
            \frac{\Delta L}{2} & 0                            & \frac{\psi_{\mathrm{pm}}}{2} \\
            0                  & \frac{\psi_{\mathrm{pm}}}{2} & -\tau
        \end{bmatrix}\bm{z}=0,
        \quad
        q_I=\bm{z}^\top
        \begin{bmatrix}
            1 & 0 & 0 \\0&1&0\\0&0&-r^2
        \end{bmatrix}\bm{z}=0 .
    \]\pause%
    MTPC means tangency of $q_T$ and the smallest admissible $q_I$:
    \[
        q_T(\bm{z})=0,
        \qquad
        \nabla q_T(\bm{z})=\lambda\nabla q_I(\bm{z}).
    \]\pause%
    Eliminating $i_{\mathrm{s,q}}$ yields the algebraic candidate equation
    \[
        i_{\mathrm{s,d}}\left(\psi_{\mathrm{pm}}+\Delta L i_{\mathrm{s,d}}\right)^3
        -\Delta L\tau^2=0,
        \qquad
        i_{\mathrm{s,q}}=\frac{\tau}{\psi_{\mathrm{pm}}+\Delta L i_{\mathrm{s,d}}} .
    \]\pause%
    The real branch is selected by torque sign, voltage/current feasibility and continuity.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Direct constrained optimization %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Numerical constrained optimization of OPS}
    Directly solve the nonlinear program via a numerical solver:
    \[
        \bm{\xi}^* \in \argmin_{\bm{\xi}} J_{\mathrm{OPS}}(\bm{\xi};\theta)
        \quad\text{s.t.}\quad
        T(\bm{\xi})=T^*,\quad \|i(\bm{\xi})\|\le i_{\max},\quad \|u(\bm{\xi})\|\le u_{\max}.
    \]\pause%
    \begin{columns}[T,totalwidth=0.98\textwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{MATLAB}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.39\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://www.mathworks.com/help/optim/ug/fmincon.html}{\texttt{fmincon}}: SQP, interior-point, active-set
                        \item \href{https://www.mathworks.com/help/gads/multistart.html}{\texttt{MultiStart}}, \href{https://www.mathworks.com/help/gads/globalsearch.html}{\texttt{GlobalSearch}}
                        \item \href{https://www.mathworks.com/help/optim/ug/lsqnonlin.html}{\texttt{lsqnonlin}} for KKT residuals
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}\pause%
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{Python / JAX}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.39\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://docs.scipy.org/doc/scipy/reference/generated/scipy.optimize.minimize.html}{SciPy \texttt{minimize}}: SLSQP, trust-constr
                        \item \href{https://web.casadi.org/docs/}{CasADi} + \href{https://coin-or.github.io/Ipopt/}{IPOPT} for AD-based NLPs
                        \item \href{https://jaxopt.github.io/}{JAXopt}: differentiable solvers and projections
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}\pause%
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{C/C++ (embedded)}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.39\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://docs.acados.org/}{acados}: SQP / SQP-RTI code generation
                        \item \href{https://github.com/giaf/hpipm}{HPIPM}: embedded QP/QCQP routines
                        \item \href{https://coin-or.github.io/qpOASES/doc/3.0/doxygen/index.html}{qpOASES} or \href{https://osqp.org/docs/}{OSQP} for SQP subproblems
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% LUT and surrogate based OPS %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{LUT-based and surrogate-based OPS}
    Let the parameter vector $\bm{\theta}$ collect the online requests and constraints:
    \[
        \bm{\theta}=(T^*,\omega,u_{\mathrm{dc}},i_{\max},\ldots),
        \qquad
        \bm{\xi}=\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\quad\text{or}\quad
        \bm{\xi}=[\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^\top\ i_{\mathrm{f}}]^\top .
    \]\pause%
    Offline, solve the OPS problem on a grid:
    \[
        \bm{\xi}_j^*\in
        \argmin_{\bm{\xi}} J_{\mathrm{OPS}}(\bm{\xi};\bm{\theta}_j)
        \quad\text{s.t.}\quad
        g(\bm{\xi};\bm{\theta}_j)=0,
        \quad
        h(\bm{\xi};\bm{\theta}_j)\le 0,
    \]\pause%
    \[
        \mathcal D_N=\{(\bm{\theta}_j,\bm{\xi}_j^*)\}_{j=1}^{N}.
    \]\pause%
    Online, replace the implicit optimizer by an explicit approximation:
    \[
        \bm{\xi}^*(\bm{\theta})\approx \widehat{\bm{\xi}}^*(\bm{\theta})
        =\mathcal I_{\mathrm{LUT}}(\bm{\theta};\mathcal D_N)
        \quad\text{or}\quad
        \widehat{\bm{\xi}}^*(\bm{\theta})=g_\eta(\bm{\theta}).
    \]
    \begin{itemize}
        \item $\mathcal I_{\mathrm{LUT}}$: nearest-neighbor, multilinear or spline interpolation.\pause%
        \item $g_\eta$: polynomial, piecewise-affine, Gaussian-process or ANN surrogate.\pause%
        \item Optional online feasibility repair: projection, clipping or fallback to a safe OPS region.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Small OPS solution methods comparison %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Small OPS solution methods comparison}
    \vspace{0.4cm}
    \begin{table}
        \centering
        \begin{tabular}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.14\textwidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.14\textwidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.30\textwidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.30\textwidth}}
            \toprule
            \hlh{Method}                       & \hlh{Real-time load} & \hlh{Pro}                                              & \hlh{Con}                                                    \\
            \midrule\addlinespace[5pt]
            Analytical roots                   & Low to medium        & Easy adaption to changing parameters                   & Additional iterative approximation step for nonlinear models \\
            \addlinespace[5pt]
            \onslide<2->Numerical optimization & Medium to high       & General purpose; adapts to new machine parameters      & Requires external solvers; Highest load                      \\
            \addlinespace[5pt]
            \onslide<3->LUT interpolation      & Very low             & Smallest online load                                   & Fixed solution; no online adaption                           \\
            \addlinespace[5pt]
            \onslide<4->Approximate function   & Low to medium        & Requires additional training step; approximation error & Eventually parallelizable (e.g., for FPGA)                   \\
            \bottomrule
        \end{tabular}
        \caption{Qualitative comparison of OPS solution methods}
        \label{tab:ops_comparison}
    \end{table}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Reading list %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{OPS solution methods: selected reading}

    \begin{columns}[T,totalwidth=0.98\textwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{Analytical / algebraic}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.38\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/TPEL.2013.2245920}{Jung, Hong and Nam (2013)}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/TPEL.2014.2354299}{Preindl and Bolognani (2015)}\item \href{https://doi.org/10.1080/00207179.2017.1338359}{Eldeeb et al. (2018)}
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}\pause%
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{Constrained / numerical}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.38\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/CCTA49430.2022.9965988}{Reinhard et al. (2022)}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/IAS62731.2025.11061499}{Houmsi et al. (2025)}
                        \item \href{https://arxiv.org/html/2604.17165}{Parson-Scherban et al. (2026)}
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}\pause%
        \begin{column}{0.30\textwidth}
            \begin{block}{LUT / data-driven}
                \begin{minipage}[t][0.38\textheight][t]{\linewidth}
                    \begin{itemize}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/IECON.2012.6389438}{Peters et al. (2012)}
                        \item \href{https://www.mdpi.com/1996-1073/15/5/1838}{B\"uttner et al. (2022)}
                        \item \href{https://doi.org/10.1109/OJIES.2024.3356721}{Monzen et al. (2024)}
                    \end{itemize}
                \end{minipage}
            \end{block}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}\pause%
    \vspace{1mm}
    \begin{varblock}{Remark}
        If correctly implemented, all methods yield the same optimal set points. The choice of method is a trade-off between real-time load, implementation effort and flexibility.
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Selected implementation example: LUT-based OPS %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Selected implementation example: LUT-based PMSM-OPS}
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{center}
            \begin{tikzpicture}[>=Latex, thick, node distance=2.5cm, align=center]
                % inputs
                \node (psimax) at (0, 3.3) {$\frac{u_\mathrm{max}}{\omega}\approx\psi_{\max}$};
                \node (tstar) at (0, 0) {\(T^*\)};
                \coordinate (tstar_tap) at (1, 0);

                % Psi_opt block
                \node[ctrlblock, minimum width=1.5cm, minimum height=1.2cm] (psiopt) at (2.25, 1.5) {};
                \begin{scope}[shift={(psiopt.center)}]
                    \draw[->, thin] (-5mm, -2mm) -- (5mm, -2mm);
                    \draw[->, thin] (0mm, -4mm) -- (0mm, 4mm);
                    \draw[color=black, thick, domain=-3.5:3.5, samples=20, variable=\x] plot ({\x mm}, {-1mm + 0.2*\x*\x mm});
                \end{scope}
                \node[below=0.1mm of psiopt] {\(\psi_{\mathrm{MTPC}}^*(T)\)};

                % min block
                \node[ctrlblock, minimum width=1.2cm, minimum height=1.2cm] (minb) at (4, 3) {min};

                % T_max block
                \node[ctrlblock, minimum width=1.5cm, minimum height=1.2cm] (tmax) at (6.25, 1.5) {};
                \begin{scope}[shift={(tmax.center)}]
                    \draw[->, thin] (-4mm, 0mm) -- (5mm, 0mm);
                    \draw[->, thin] (-2mm, -4mm) -- (-2mm, 4mm);
                    \draw[color=black, thick, domain=-3.5:3.5, samples=20, variable=\y] plot ({-2mm + 0.4*\y*\y mm}, {\y mm});
                \end{scope}
                \node[below=0.1mm of tmax] {\(T_{\max}(\psi)\)};

                % limiter (saturation)
                \node[ctrlblock, minimum width=1.2cm, minimum height=1.2cm] (lim) at (7.75, 0) {};
                \draw[-, thick] ([yshift=-2mm,xshift=-3mm]lim.center) -- ([yshift=-2mm,xshift=-1mm]lim.center) -- ([yshift=2mm,xshift=1mm]lim.center) -- ([yshift=2mm,xshift=3mm]lim.center);
                \node[right=2mm of lim, yshift=-4mm] {\(T_{\mathrm{lim}}^*\)};

                % f(psi, T)
                \node[ctrlblock, minimum width=0.8cm, minimum height=4cm] (fblock2) at (10.25, 1.5) {\rotatebox{90}{$f(\psi, T)$}};

                % connections
                \draw[->] (psimax) -- (minb.west |- psimax);
                \draw[-] (tstar) -- (tstar_tap);
                \draw[->] (tstar_tap) |- (psiopt.west);
                \draw[->] (tstar_tap) -- (lim.west);

                \draw[->] (psiopt.north) |- ([yshift=-3mm]minb.west);

                \draw[->] (minb.east) -- (fblock2.west |- minb.east) node[near end, above, xshift=4mm] {\(\psi_{\mathrm{lim}}^*\)};

                \coordinate (psilim_tap) at (5, 3);
                \fill (psilim_tap) circle(1.5pt);
                \draw[->] (psilim_tap) |- (tmax.west);

                \draw[->] (tmax.east) -| (lim.north);

                \draw[->] (lim.east) -- (fblock2.west |- lim.east);

                \draw[->] (fblock2.east |- minb.west) -- +(1,0) node[right] {\(i_{\mathrm{s,d}}^*\ \)};
                \draw[->] (fblock2.east |- tstar) -- +(1,0) node[right] {\(i_{\mathrm{s,q}}^*\ \)};

                \fill (tstar_tap) circle(1.5pt);
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \end{center}
        \caption{LUT-based OPS implementation: first calculated required flux magntitude $\psi_{\mathrm{MTPC}}^*(T^*)$ in MTPC mode, then check if available voltage (and thus flux $\psi_\mathrm{max}$) is sufficient to achieve the torque. Limit flux and torque in flux weakening mode if necessary (following MC and MTPV mode). Finally, $\psi_\mathrm{lim}^*$ and $T_{\mathrm{lim}}^*$ represents a feasible operating point which is then transformed to the current plane.}
        \label{fig:LUT_OPS}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Selected implementation example: LUT-based OPS (cont.)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Selected implementation example: LUT-based PMSM-OPS (cont.)}
    \begin{columns}[c,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.50\textwidth}
            \begin{center}
                \begin{tikzpicture}
                    \begin{axis}[
                            width=8.0cm,
                            height=5.5cm,
                            xmin=-1.05,xmax=1.05,
                            ymin=0,ymax=1.08,
                            xlabel={$T^*/T_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                            ylabel={$\psi^*_{\mathrm{MTPC}}/\psi_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                            grid=major,
                            legend style={draw=black, fill=white, at={(0.5,0.05)}, anchor=south},
                        ]
                        \addplot[very thick, color=signalbeta, domain=-\lutyR:\lutyR, samples=240, variable=\y]
                        ({luttorquenorm(xmtpcnorm(\y),\y)},{lutfluxnorm(xmtpcnorm(\y),\y)});
                        \addlegendentry{$i^*\in\mathbb{MTPC}$}
                    \end{axis}
                \end{tikzpicture}
            \end{center}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.45\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item This LUT stores the required flux magnitude $\psi^*_{\mathrm{MTPC}}$ to achieve the requested torque $T^*$ in MTPC mode:
                      $$
                          i^*_{\mathrm{MTPC}}(T^*)
                          \in
                          \arg\min_{T(\bm{i})=T^*}\|\bm{i}\|_2^2
                      $$
                      $$
                          \psi^*_{\mathrm{MTPC}}(T^*)
                          =
                          \left\|\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\bigl(i^*_{\mathrm{MTPC}}(T^*)\bigr)\right\|_2 .
                      $$
                \item In low-speed operation, this map supplies the requested flux before voltage saturation.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Selected implementation example: LUT-based OPS (cont.)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Selected implementation example: LUT-based PMSM-OPS (cont.)}
    \begin{columns}[c,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.50\textwidth}
            \begin{center}
                \begin{tikzpicture}
                    \begin{axis}[
                            width=8.0cm,
                            height=5.5cm,
                            xmin=0,xmax=1.05,
                            ymin=0,ymax=1.08,
                            xlabel={$\psi_{\mathrm{lim}}/\psi_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                            ylabel={$T_{\lim}/T_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                            grid=major,
                            legend style={draw=black, fill=white, at={(0.04,0.96)}, anchor=north west, legend cell align=left},
                        ]
                        \addplot[very thick, color=signalgamma, domain=0.001:\lutyM, samples=180, variable=\y]
                        ({lutfluxnorm(xmtpvnorm(\y),\y)},{luttorquenorm(xmtpvnorm(\y),\y)});
                        \addlegendentry{$i^*\in\mathbb{MTPV}$}
                        \addplot[very thick, color=signaldelta, domain=\lutyM:\lutyR, samples=180, variable=\y]
                        ({lutfluxnorm(xcurrentnorm(\y),\y)},{luttorquenorm(xcurrentnorm(\y),\y)});
                        \addlegendentry{$i^*\in\mathbb{MC}$}
                        \addplot[only marks, mark=square*, mark size=4, color=signalgamma]
                        coordinates {({lutfluxnorm(\lutxM,\lutyM)},{luttorquenorm(\lutxM,\lutyM)})};
                    \end{axis}
                \end{tikzpicture}
            \end{center}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.46\textwidth}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item For some given limited stator flux
                      $$
                          \psi_{\mathrm{lim}}\approx\nicefrac{u_{\mathrm{max}}}{\omega},
                      $$
                      this LUT stores the maximum achievable torque $T_{\lim}$
                      $$
                          T_{\lim}(\psi_{\mathrm{lim}})=\max_{\bm{i}}\,T(\bm{i})
                      $$
                      under voltage and current constraints:
                      $$\text{s.t.}\quad
                          \|\bm{\psi}(\bm{i})\|_2\le \psi_{\mathrm{lim}},\quad
                          \|\bm{i}\|_2\le i_{\mathrm{max}} .
                      $$
                \item In high-speed operation, this maps the MTPV and MC regions into the flux-torque space.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Selected implementation example: LUT-based OPS (cont.)
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Selected implementation example: LUT-based PMSM-OPS (cont.)}
    \begin{figure}
        \centering
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{axis}[
                    width=0.45\textwidth,
                    height=0.7\textheight,
                    view={120}{24},
                    xmin=-1.02, xmax=1.02,
                    ymin=0.0, ymax=1.02,
                    zmin=-0.95, zmax=0.05,
                    xlabel={$T/T_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                    ylabel={$|\psi|/\psi_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                    zlabel={$i^*_{\mathrm{s,d}}/i_{\mathrm{s,max}}$},
                    grid=major,
                    mesh/rows=65,
                    shader=interp,
                    faceted color=none,
                    colormap name=T-S-IR,
                    tick label style={font=\scriptsize},
                    label style={font=\scriptsize},
                ]
                \addplot3[surf] table[x index=0,y index=1,z index=2] {fig/lec03/lut_inverse_id.dat};
            \end{axis}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \hfill
        \begin{tikzpicture}
            \begin{axis}[
                    width=0.45\textwidth,
                    height=0.7\textheight,
                    view={120}{24},
                    xmin=-1.02, xmax=1.02,
                    ymin=0.0, ymax=1.02,
                    zmin=-0.85, zmax=0.85,
                    xlabel={$T/T_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                    ylabel={$|\psi|/\psi_{\mathrm{max}}$},
                    zlabel={$i^*_{\mathrm{s,q}}/i_{\mathrm{s,max}}$},
                    grid=major,
                    mesh/rows=65,
                    shader=interp,
                    faceted color=none,
                    colormap name=T-S-IR,
                    tick label style={font=\scriptsize},
                    label style={font=\scriptsize},
                ]
                \addplot3[surf] table[x index=0,y index=1,z index=2] {fig/lec03/lut_inverse_iq.dat};
            \end{axis}
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{Exemplary flux-torque-to-current mapping $\left\{i_\mathrm{s,d}^*, i_\mathrm{s,q}^*\right\} = f(\psi_\mathrm{lim}, T_\mathrm{lim})$ in the feasible operating region}
        \label{fig:lut_inverse_surfaces}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsubsection{Modulation degree control}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Modulation degree control structure %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Modulation degree control structure}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{circuitikz}[>=Latex, scale=0.75, transform shape]
            \tikzset{
                detailblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.34cm, minimum height=1.02cm, font=\small},
                intblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.10cm, minimum height=1.02cm, font=\small},
                tfblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=2.00cm, minimum height=1.90cm, inner sep=0pt},
                dublock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.72cm, minimum height=1.48cm, font=\small},
                satblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=1.64cm, minimum height=1.98cm, inner sep=0pt},
                sig/.style = {font=\small, inner sep=1.5pt},
                tap/.style = {circle, fill=black, inner sep=1.15pt}
            }
            \ctikzset{block left anchors pos=0.7, block right anchors pos=0.7}
            \def\phaseport{0.72}
            \def\smallgap{0.6cm}
            \def\medgap{1.0cm}
            \def\biggap{2.25cm}

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumd) {};

            \coordinate[left=\smallgap of sumd] (refd);
            \draw[->, thick] (refd) -- (sumd.west);
            \node[sig, above] at ($(refd)!0.1!(sumd.west)$) {$m^{*}$};

            \coordinate[below=\smallgap of sumd.south] (fbd);
            \draw[->, thick] (fbd) -- (fbd |- sumd.south);
            \node[sig, left] at ($(fbd)!0.10!(fbd |- sumd.south)$) {$m$};


            \node[detailblock, right=\medgap of sumd] (kpd) {$K_{\mathrm{p,m}}$};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of kpd] (kid);

            \draw[->, thick] (sumd) -- (kpd);


            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$-$}, above=0.5cm of kpd] (sumid) {};
            \draw[->, thick] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) to[short, *-] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) |-  (sumid.west);

            \node[intblock, right=\smallgap of sumid] (intd) {$\dfrac{\mathrm{z}T_\mathrm{s}}{\mathrm{z}-1}$};


            \draw[->, thick] (sumid.east) -- (intd.west);

            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of intd] (kid2) {$K_{\mathrm{i,m}}$};
            \draw[->, thick] (intd.east) -- (kid2.west);

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$}, right=\smallgap of kid2] (sumvd) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (kid2.east) -- (sumvd.west);
            \draw[->, thick] (kpd.east) -| (sumvd.south);


            \node[saturationshape, right=\smallgap of sumvd] (saturation) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumvd.east) -- (saturation.left);

            \draw[thick, ->] (saturation.right) -- node[sig, pos=0.4, below, yshift=-4mm]{$\Delta \psi$} ++(\smallgap, 0) coordinate (out_delta_psi);

            \node[twoportshape, anchor=south, t=$\Delta u$] (delta) at ($(sumvd.east)!0.25!(saturation.west)+(0,1.25cm)$) {};
            \coordinate (deltaBottomB) at ($(delta.south west)!0.5!(delta.south east)$);
            \coordinate (deltaTapB) at (deltaBottomB |- saturation.west);
            \draw[->, thick] (sumvd.east) -- (deltaTapB) to [short, *-] (deltaBottomB);

            %define equivalent DeltaTap coordinates at the east side of the delta block for drawing the feedback lines
            \coordinate (deltaEastB) at ($(delta.north east)!0.5!(delta.south east)$);



            \node[detailblock] (kawd) at (kid2 |- delta.west) {$K_{\mathrm{aw,m}}$};
            \draw[->, thick] (delta.west) -- (kawd.east);
            \draw[->, thick] (kawd.west) -| (sumid.north);

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}, anchor=west] (sumpsi) at (out_delta_psi){};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of sumpsi.north] (fbpsi);
            \draw[->, thick] (fbpsi) -- (fbpsi |- sumpsi.north);
            \node[sig, right, anchor=west] at ($(fbpsi)!0.10!(fbpsi |- sumpsi.north)$) {$\psi'_{\mathrm{max}}$};
            \draw[->, thick] ($(saturation.east)!0.25!(sumpsi.west)$) to [short, *-] ($(saturation.east)!0.25!(sumpsi.west)$) |- (deltaEastB);

            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of sumpsi] (OPS) {OPS};
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$-$}, right=\smallgap of OPS] (sumcc) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumpsi.east) --node[sig, below, yshift=-4mm]{$\psi_\mathrm{max}$} (OPS.west);
            \draw[->, thick] (OPS.east) -- node[sig, below, yshift=-4mm]{$\bm{i}^*_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$} (sumcc.west);

            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of sumcc] (CC) {Current\\ controller};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumcc.east) -- (CC.west);
            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of CC] (MA) {Machine};
            \draw[->, thick] (CC.east) -- (MA.west);
            \draw[->,thick] (MA.east) -- node[sig, pos=0.4, below]{$\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$} ++(\medgap, 0) coordinate (out_idq);
            \coordinate (out_feedback_back) at ($(out_idq)!0.5!(out_idq -| MA.east)$);
            \draw[->, thick] (MA.east) -- (out_feedback_back) to [short, *-] (delta.east -| out_feedback_back) -| (sumcc.north);
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/east={$*$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$/$}] (summ) at (fbd -| sumpsi.north){};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of summ.north] (fbudc);
            \draw[->, thick] (fbudc) -- (fbudc |- summ.north);
            \node[sig, right, anchor=west] at ($(fbudc)!0.10!(fbudc |- summ.north)$) {$\nicefrac{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}}{\sqrt{3}}$};
            \node[detailblock] (abs) at (kawd |- summ) {$||\bm{x}||_2$};
            \draw[->, thick] ($(CC.east)!0.25!(MA.west)$) to [short, *-] ($(CC.east)!0.25!(MA.west)$) |- node[sig, left, yshift=2mm, xshift=-1mm]{$\bm{u}^*_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$} (summ.east);
            \draw[->, thick] (summ.west) -- (abs.east);
            \draw[->, thick] (abs.west) -| (sumd.south);

        \end{circuitikz}%
        \caption{Modulation degree controller  with ARW (this is not a classical outer control loop structure as the modulation degree control feedback signal is the actuation signal of the inner current controller)}
        \label{fig:modulation_degree_control}
    \end{figure}
    \vspace{-0.65cm}
    \begin{varblock}{Motivation for modulation degree control}
        The FOC's decoupling works only properly in the linear modulation range ($m^* \leq \nicefrac{2}{\sqrt{3}}$) as otherwise voltage clipping will distort the current controller. Considering the uncertainty due to both the inverter nonlinearity and the machine parameters, an active control is required to ensure that the reference modulation degree is met.
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Control approach and plant definition %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Control approach and plant definition}
    The modulation index is estimated based on the current controller's reference voltage vector $\bm{u}^*_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$ and the DC-link voltage $u_{\mathrm{dc}}$:
    \begin{equation}
        m = \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \frac{\|\bm{u}^*_{\mathrm{s,dq}}\|_2}{u_{\mathrm{dc}}} .
    \end{equation}
    The modulation controller generates an \hl{additive correction of the admissible flux limit}:
    \begin{equation}
        \psi_{\max} = \psi'_{\max} + \Delta\psi,
        \qquad
        \psi'_{\max} = \frac{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}}{\sqrt{3}|\omega|} .
    \end{equation}
    Here, $\psi'_{\max}$ is the nominal flux limit (neglecting the inverter nonlinearity and the ohmic voltage drop) and $\Delta\psi$ is the correction term generated by the modulation degree controller.    For a fixed operating point $(T^*,\omega,u_{\mathrm{dc}})$ and an unchanged OPS active set, the local plant is
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},m}(\mathrm{z}) = \frac{\Delta M(\mathrm{z})}{\Delta \Psi(\mathrm{z})} .
    \end{equation}
    Hence, the \hl{plant input} is the flux correction $\Delta\psi$ and the \hl{plant output} is the modulation index.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Local OPS linearization %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Local OPS linearization in flux weakening}
    We consider the simplified PMSM model with constant inductance matrix
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} = \bm{L}\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} + \bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{PM}},
        \qquad
        \bm{L} =
        \begin{bmatrix}
            L_{\mathrm{dd}} & 0               \\
            0               & L_{\mathrm{qq}}
        \end{bmatrix},
        \qquad
        \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} = R_{\mathrm{s}}\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} + \omega\bm{J}\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s,dq}} .
    \end{equation}
    In regular flux-weakening operation, the local OPS solution $\bar{\bm{i}}^*$ is characterized by the active constraints
    \begin{equation}
        T(\bar{\bm{i}}^*) = T^*,
        \qquad
        U(\bar{\bm{i}}^*,\omega) = \|\bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bar{\bm{i}}^*,\omega)\|_2 = |\omega|\psi_{\max} .
    \end{equation}
    Linearization yields
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{bmatrix}
            \bar{\bm{T}}_i\T \\
            \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T
        \end{bmatrix}
        \Delta \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*
        =
        \begin{bmatrix}
            0 \\
            |\omega|
        \end{bmatrix}
        \Delta \psi .
    \end{equation}
    Therefore, we receive
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^* = \bar{\bm{h}}\,\Delta \psi,
        \qquad
        \bar{\bm{h}} =
        \begin{bmatrix}
            \bar{\bm{T}}_i\T \\
            \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T
        \end{bmatrix}^{-1}
        \begin{bmatrix}
            0 \\
            |\omega|
        \end{bmatrix} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Sensitivities %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Interpretation of the local sensitivities}
    The quantities in the local OPS model are
    \begin{equation}
        \bar{\bm{T}}_i = \left.\frac{\partial T}{\partial \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}\right|_{\bar{\bm{i}}^*},
        \qquad
        \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T = \left.\frac{\partial U}{\partial \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}\right|_{\bar{\bm{i}}^*} .
    \end{equation}
    For the constant-inductance model, the voltage Jacobian becomes
    \begin{equation}
        \bar{\bm{A}}_u
        = \left.\frac{\partial \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}{\partial \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}}\right|_{\bar{\bm{i}}^*}
        = R_{\mathrm{s}}\bm{I} + \omega\bm{J}\bm{L} .
    \end{equation}
    With $\bar{\bm{u}} = \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bar{\bm{i}}^*,\omega)$, the voltage-magnitude gradient is
    \begin{equation}
        \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T = \frac{\bar{\bm{u}}\T}{\|\bar{\bm{u}}\|_2}\,\bar{\bm{A}}_u .
    \end{equation}
    Thus, $\bar{\bm{h}}$ is the \hl{local current-reference direction} imposed by the OPS when the admissible flux correction is perturbed at constant torque.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Static gain %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Static gain of the plant}
    The local variation of the voltage magnitude is
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta U = \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T\Delta \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*
        = \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T\bar{\bm{h}}\,\Delta \psi .
    \end{equation}
    From the second row of the OPS linearization it follows directly that
    \begin{equation}
        \bar{\bm{U}}_i\T\bar{\bm{h}} = |\omega| .
    \end{equation}
    Hence,
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta m = \frac{\Delta U}{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}/\sqrt{3}}
        = \frac{|\omega|\sqrt{3}}{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}}\,\Delta \psi .
    \end{equation}
    The \hl{static plant gain} is therefore
    \begin{equation}
        K_{m} = \frac{\Delta m}{\Delta \psi}
        = \frac{|\omega|\sqrt{3}}{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Dynamic part %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Dynamic part: voltage demand of the current controller}
    The modulation feedback is not based on the current response, but on the voltage demand at the current-controller output:
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta \bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \bm{G}_{u i^*}(\mathrm{z})\Delta \bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}^*(\mathrm{z}) .
    \end{equation}
    With the local voltage-vector direction
    \begin{equation}
        \bar{\bm{n}}_u =
        \frac{\bar{\bm{u}}}{\|\bar{\bm{u}}\|_2},
        \qquad
        \bar{\bm{u}}=\bm{u}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}(\bar{\bm{i}}^*,\omega),
    \end{equation}
    the local plant seen by the modulation controller is
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},m}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \frac{1}{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}/\sqrt{3}}\,
        \bar{\bm{n}}_u\T\bm{G}_{u i^*}(\mathrm{z})\bar{\bm{h}}.
    \end{equation}
    Due to the inner current loop having zero stationary tracking error, the static gain remains
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},m}(1)
        =
        K_{m}
        =
        \frac{|\omega|\sqrt{3}}{2u_{\mathrm{dc}}} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Discrete-time PT1 reduction %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Scalar lead-lag approximation of the plant}
    For one decoupled current-control axis, consider the discrete current plant
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},\nu}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \frac{I_\nu(\mathrm{z})}{U_\nu(\mathrm{z})}
        =
        \frac{b_\nu}{\mathrm{z}-a_\nu},
        \qquad \nu\in\{\mathrm{d},\mathrm{q}\} .
    \end{equation}
    If the closed current-reference response is approximated by (e.g., due to pole-zero cancellation in the current loop design)
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{i},\nu}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \frac{I_\nu(\mathrm{z})}{I_\nu^*(\mathrm{z})}
        \approx
        \frac{1-\lambda_\nu}{\mathrm{z}-\lambda_\nu},
    \end{equation}
    with $\lambda_\nu$ representing the designed pole location, then the voltage-demand response is
    \begin{equation}
        G_{u i^*,\nu}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \frac{U_\nu(\mathrm{z})}{I_\nu^*(\mathrm{z})}
        \approx
        \frac{\mathrm{z}-a_\nu}{b_\nu}
        \frac{1-\lambda_\nu}{\mathrm{z}-\lambda_\nu} .
    \end{equation}
    After projection onto the local voltage direction, we use the following lead-lag approximation
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},m}(\mathrm{z})
        \approx
        K_{m}\frac{1-\lambda_u}{1-a_u}
        \frac{\mathrm{z}-a_u}{\mathrm{z}-\lambda_u} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Discrete-time PI controller %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Discrete-time PI modulation controller}
    The modulation-control error is defined analogously to the current-control error:
    \begin{equation}
        e_m[k] = m^*[k]-m[k] .
    \end{equation}
    The unlimited controller output is the flux-correction command
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\Psi^{*}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        G_{\mathrm{c},m}(\mathrm{z})E_m(\mathrm{z}) .
    \end{equation}
    Using the same PI structure as used for the current loops,
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{c},m}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        K_{\mathrm{p},m}
        +
        K_{\mathrm{i},m}T_{\mathrm{s}}\frac{\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-1}
        =
        k_m\frac{\mathrm{z}-z_m}{\mathrm{z}-1}.
    \end{equation}
    we find the following relationships between the controller parameters:
    \begin{equation}
        k_m=K_{\mathrm{p},m}+K_{\mathrm{i},m}T_{\mathrm{s}},
        \qquad
        z_m=
        \frac{K_{\mathrm{p},m}}{K_{\mathrm{p},m}+K_{\mathrm{i},m}T_{\mathrm{s}}}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% PI gain design %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Pole-placement design for the PI controller}
    Use the scalar voltage-demand plant
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{p},m}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \gamma_u\frac{\mathrm{z}-a_u}{\mathrm{z}-\lambda_u},
        \qquad
        \gamma_u=
        K_{m}\frac{1-\lambda_u}{1-a_u},
    \end{equation}
    with
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{c},m}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        k_m\frac{\mathrm{z}-z_m}{\mathrm{z}-1},
    \end{equation}
    the closed-loop characteristic polynomial is
    \begin{equation}
        (\mathrm{z}-1)(\mathrm{z}-\lambda_u)
        +
        \kappa(\mathrm{z}-a_u)(\mathrm{z}-z_m)
        =
        0,
        \qquad
        \kappa=k_m\gamma_u .
    \end{equation}
    This directly places the two modulation-loop poles while accounting for the zero generated by the current-controller voltage demand.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gain parameters and bandwidth separation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{PI gains from desired modulation-loop poles}
    Choose the desired poles $p_1,p_2$ \hl{significantly slower} than the current-control dynamics\footnote{Otherwise, unwanted interactions between the loops may occur.}, e.g.,
    \begin{equation}
        p_1=p_2=\lambda_m,
        \qquad
        \lambda_m=\mathrm{e}^{-\rho_m},
        \qquad
        \rho_m=\frac{\rho}{\alpha},
        \qquad
        \alpha\in[5,15] .
    \end{equation}
    Define
    \begin{equation}
        a_{\mathrm{d}}=p_1+p_2,
        \qquad
        b_{\mathrm{d}}=p_1p_2,
        \qquad
        N=a_{\mathrm{d}}-(1+\lambda_u),
        \qquad
        M=b_{\mathrm{d}}-\lambda_u .
    \end{equation}
    The PI zero and gain factor follow from coefficient comparison:
    \begin{equation}
        z_m=
        \frac{M(a_u-a_{\mathrm{d}})+Nb_{\mathrm{d}}}{Na_u-M},
        \qquad
        \kappa=
        \frac{N}{a_u+z_m-a_{\mathrm{d}}}.
    \end{equation}
    Finally,
    \begin{equation}
        k_m=\frac{\kappa}{\gamma_u},
        \qquad
        K_{\mathrm{p},m}=k_mz_m,
        \qquad
        K_{\mathrm{i},m}=
        \frac{k_m(1-z_m)}{T_{\mathrm{s}}}.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Flux correction limits %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Flux correction limits}
    The unlimited controller output is limited before it enters the OPS:
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\psi_v[k]
        = \mathrm{lim}_{\Delta\psi_{v,\min}}^{\Delta\psi_{v,\max}}\left\{\Delta\psi_v^{*}[k]\right\} .
    \end{equation}
    A simple calibration rule is to use fixed correction limits relative to the maximum nominal flux linkage:
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\psi_{v,\max}=+\varepsilon_\psi\psi_{\mathrm{s},\max}^{\mathrm{nom}},
        \qquad
        \Delta\psi_{v,\min}=-\varepsilon_\psi\psi_{\mathrm{s},\max}^{\mathrm{nom}},
        \qquad
        \varepsilon_\psi \approx 0.1 .
    \end{equation}
    \begin{varblock}{Motivation for flux correction limits}
        Outside flux weakening, the modulation degree is below the reference value, i.e., $m < m^*$. Hence, the modulation controller is driven toward the positive correction limit trying to increase the admissible flux (which should be without any impact because the modulation controller is practically off in the MTPC region). Once flux weakening is entered, the modulation controller should leave the positive limit and start regulating the modulation degree which is why the positive limit should be not too large.
    \end{varblock}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% ARW feedback implementation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{ARW feedback for the modulation controller}
    The unlimited integral action is
    \begin{equation}
        x_{\mathrm{i},m}^{+}[k]
        =x_{\mathrm{i},m}[k-1]+T_{\mathrm{s}}e_m[k],
        \qquad
        \psi_{\mathrm{i},m}^{+}[k]=K_{\mathrm{i},m}x_{\mathrm{i},m}^{+}[k] .
    \end{equation}
    The unlimited PI output and its limited value are
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta\psi_v^{*}[k]=K_{\mathrm{p},m}e_m[k]+\psi_{\mathrm{i},m}^{+}[k],
        \qquad
        \Delta\psi_v[k]
        =\mathrm{lim}_{\Delta\psi_{v,\min}}^{\Delta\psi_{v,\max}}\left\{\Delta\psi_v^{*}[k]\right\} .
    \end{equation}
    The saturation mismatch is
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta u[k]=\Delta\psi_v^{*}[k]-\Delta\psi_v[k] .
    \end{equation}
    The ARW feedback corrects the integrator state according to
    \begin{equation}
        x_{\mathrm{i},m}[k]
        =x_{\mathrm{i},m}^{+}[k]
        -\frac{K_{\mathrm{aw},m}}{K_{\mathrm{i},m}}\Delta u[k],
        \qquad
        \psi_{\mathrm{i},m}[k]=K_{\mathrm{i},m}x_{\mathrm{i},m}[k] .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% ARW dynamics %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{ARW tracking dynamics}
    The integral flux correction becomes
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            \psi_{\mathrm{i},m}[k]
             & =(1-K_{\mathrm{aw},m})\psi_{\mathrm{i},m}[k-1]                                                            \\
             & +\left[(1-K_{\mathrm{aw},m})K_{\mathrm{i},m}T_{\mathrm{s}}-K_{\mathrm{aw},m}K_{\mathrm{p},m}\right]e_m[k]
            +K_{\mathrm{aw},m}\Delta\psi_v[k] .
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}
    For the isolated ARW tracking dynamics, i.e., $e_m[k]=0$,
    \begin{equation}
        \psi_{\mathrm{i},m}[k]
        =(1-K_{\mathrm{aw},m})\psi_{\mathrm{i},m}[k-1]
        +K_{\mathrm{aw},m}\Delta\psi_v[k] .
    \end{equation}
    Hence,
    \begin{equation}
        \frac{\Psi_{\mathrm{i},m}(\mathrm{z})}{\Delta\Psi_v(\mathrm{z})}
        =\frac{K_{\mathrm{aw},m}\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-(1-K_{\mathrm{aw},m})},
        \qquad
        \lambda_{\mathrm{aw},m}=1-K_{\mathrm{aw},m} .
    \end{equation}
    A practical choice is $\lambda_{\mathrm{aw},m}\leq\lambda_m$, i.e., ARW tracking at least as fast as the modulation loop.
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Direct torque control}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Direct torque control: high-level overview %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Direct torque control (DTC): high-level overview}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{circuitikz}[x=1cm, y=1cm, scale=0.91, transform shape, >=Latex]
            \def\dtcblockheight{1.5cm}
            \def\dtcblockgaplarge{1.20cm}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\dtcconverterscale}{\dtcblockheight/(1.4cm*0.7)}
            \tikzset{
                dtcblock/.style = {
                        ctrlblock,
                        align = center,
                        inner sep = 3pt,
                        minimum height = \dtcblockheight,
                        font = \small
                    },
                siglabel/.style = {font = \small, inner sep = 2pt}
            }
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumT) {};
            \node[left=1.25cm of sumT] (T0) {};
            \draw[thick, ->] (T0) -- node[above, at start, anchor = south west] {$T^*$} (sumT.west);
            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}, below right = 0.6cm and 0.75cm of sumT] (sumPsi) {};
            \node (Psi0) at (T0 |- sumPsi) {};
            \draw[thick, ->] (Psi0) -- node[above, at start, anchor = south west] {$\|\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s}}\|^*$} (sumPsi.west);
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpPsi, thick] at (sumPsi.west -| sumT.south) {};
            \node[hystcontrollershape, right = \dtcblockgaplarge of sumPsi] (hyst1) {};
            \node[hystcontrollershape] at (hyst1.north |- sumT.east) (hyst2) {};
            \draw[thick, ->] (sumT.east) -- node[above, near start]{$\Delta T$} (hyst2.west);
            \draw[thick, ->] (sumPsi.east) -- node[above]{$\Delta\|\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s}}\|$} (hyst1.west);
            \node[dtcblock, minimum width = 2.0cm, minimum height = 3.3cm, right = \dtcblockgaplarge of hyst2.north east, anchor = north west, align = center] (swTab) {Switching\\table};
            \node[dtcblock, minimum width = 2.0cm, minimum height = 3.3cm, below = 0.5cm of swTab, align = center] (Est) {Torque \\ \& \\ flux \\ estimator};
            \draw[thick, ->] (hyst2.east)  -- ($(hyst2.east -| swTab.west)$);
            \draw[thick, ->] (hyst1.east)  -- ($(hyst1.east -| swTab.west)$);

            \node[tdcacshape, right = 2*\dtcblockgaplarge of swTab.north east, anchor = north west,circuitikz/blocks/scale = \dtcconverterscale]  (conv) {};
            \node[threephasemotorshaftshape, below = 3 cm of conv.south, anchor = center, circuitikz/blocks/scale = \dtcconverterscale
            ] (motor) {};

            \draw[thick] (conv.south) to[currtap, name=ctdc] (motor.north);
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterTop) at ($(conv.south)+(0.5,0)$);
            \path[name path = motorcircle] (motor.center) circle[radius = \dimexpr\dtcblockheight/2\relax];
            \path[name path = ctdcQuarterLine] (ctdcQuarterTop) -- ($(ctdcQuarterTop |- motor.south)+(0,-0.2)$);
            \path[name intersections = {of = motorcircle and ctdcQuarterLine, by = ctdcQuarterBottom}];
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterTapTop) at ($(ctdcQuarterTop)!0.05!(ctdcQuarterBottom)$);
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterTapBottom) at ($(ctdcQuarterTop)!0.4!(ctdcQuarterBottom)$);
            \draw[thick](ctdcQuarterTop) -- (ctdcQuarterTapTop);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterTapTop) to[currtap, name=ctdcquarter] (ctdcQuarterTapBottom);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterTapBottom) -- (ctdcQuarterBottom);
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterLeftTop) at ($(conv.south)+(-0.5,0)$);
            \path[name path = ctdcQuarterLeftLine] (ctdcQuarterLeftTop) -- ($(ctdcQuarterLeftTop |- motor.south)+(0,-0.2)$);
            \path[name intersections = {of = motorcircle and ctdcQuarterLeftLine, by = ctdcQuarterLeftBottom}];
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterLeftTapTop) at ($(ctdcQuarterLeftTop)!0.525!(ctdcQuarterLeftBottom)$);
            \coordinate (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom) at ($(ctdcQuarterLeftTop)!0.875!(ctdcQuarterLeftBottom)$);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTop) -- (ctdcQuarterLeftTapTop);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapTop) to[currtap, name=ctdcquarterleft] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom);
            \draw[thick] (ctdcQuarterLeftTapBottom) -- (ctdcQuarterLeftBottom);

            \coordinate (dtcVoltSenseInA) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.125!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcVoltSenseInB) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.25!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcVoltSenseInC) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.375!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcCurrSenseInA) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.5!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcCurrSenseInB) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.625!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcCurrSenseInC) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.75!(Est.south east)$);
            \coordinate (dtcMotorSense) at ($(Est.north  east)!0.875!(Est.south east)$);


            \coordinate (VoltSenseCEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.429!(conv.north west)$);
            \coordinate (VoltSenseBEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.286!(conv.north west)$);
            \coordinate (VoltSenseAEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.143!(conv.north west)$);
            \coordinate (CurrSenseAEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.571!(conv.north west)$);
            \coordinate (CurrSenseBEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.714!(conv.north west)$);
            \coordinate (CurrSenseCEdge) at ($(swTab.north east)!0.857!(conv.north west)$);

            \node[crossingshape, name = jumpiB, thick] at (ctdcquarter.tap -| conv.south) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name = jumpiC, thick] at (ctdcquarter.tap -| ctdcQuarterLeftTop) {};
            \node[crossingshape, name = jumpiC2, thick] at (ctdc.tap -| ctdcQuarterLeftTop) {};

            \draw[thick] (ctdcquarter.tap) -- (jumpiB.east);
            \draw[thick] (jumpiB.west) -- (jumpiC.east);
            \draw[thick, ->] (jumpiC.west) -| node[above, near end ] {$i_\mathrm{a}$} ($(CurrSenseAEdge |- ctdcquarter.tap)$) |- (dtcCurrSenseInA);
            \draw[thick] (ctdc.tap) -- (jumpiC2.east);
            \draw[thick, ->] (jumpiC2.west) -| node[above, near end ] {$i_\mathrm{b}$} ($(CurrSenseBEdge |- ctdc.tap)$) |- (dtcCurrSenseInB);
            \draw[thick, ->] (ctdcquarterleft.tap) -| node[above, near end ] {$i_\mathrm{c}$} ($(CurrSenseCEdge |- ctdcquarterleft.tap)$) |- (dtcCurrSenseInC);

            \draw[thick, ->] (motor.south) |- node[above left] {$\omega$} (dtcMotorSense);

            \coordinate (swTabOut) at ($(swTab.east |- conv.west)$);

            \foreach \dy/\phase in {0.5/a, 0.00/b, -0.5/c} {
                    \draw[thick, ->] ($(swTabOut)+(0,\dy)$) -- ($(conv.west)+(0,\dy)$) coordinate (convS\phase);
                    \node[siglabel, above] at ($($(swTabOut)+(0,\dy)$)!0.5!($(conv.west)+(0,\dy)$)$) {$s_\mathrm{\phase}$};
                }
            \coordinate (TorqueEstOut) at ($(Est.north  west)!0.75!(Est.south west)$);
            \coordinate (FluxEstOut) at ($(Est.north  west)!0.5!(Est.south west)$);
            \coordinate (AuxEstOut) at ($(Est.north  west)!0.25!(Est.south west)$);
            \coordinate (AuxSwIn) at ($(swTab.north  west)!0.85!(swTab.south west)$);

            \draw[thick] (TorqueEstOut)  -| node[at start, anchor = south east] {$\hat{T}$} (jumpPsi.west);
            \draw[thick, ->] (jumpPsi.east) -- (sumT.south);
            \draw[thick, ->] (FluxEstOut)  -| node[at start, anchor = south east] {$\|\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\mathrm{s}}\|$} (sumPsi.south);
            \draw[thick, ->] (AuxEstOut)   -- node[at start, anchor = south east] {$\omega, \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\mathrm{s},\upalpha\upbeta}$} ($(AuxEstOut -| hyst1.south)$) |-   (AuxSwIn);

            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpSb, thick] at (convSb -| VoltSenseAEdge) {};
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpSc, thick] at (convSc -| VoltSenseAEdge) {};
            \node[crossingshape, rotate=-90, name = jumpSc2, thick] at (convSc -| VoltSenseBEdge) {};

            \draw[thick] ($(VoltSenseAEdge |- convSa)$) to [short, *-] (jumpSb.west);
            \draw[thick] (jumpSb.east) -- (jumpSc.west);
            \draw[thick, ->] (jumpSc.east) |- (dtcVoltSenseInA);
            \draw[thick] ($(VoltSenseBEdge |- convSb)$) to [short, *-] (jumpSc2.west);
            \draw[thick, ->] (jumpSc2.east) |- (dtcVoltSenseInB);
            \draw[thick, ->] ($(VoltSenseCEdge |- convSc)$) to [short, *-] ($(VoltSenseCEdge |- convSc)$) |- (dtcVoltSenseInC);
        \end{circuitikz}
        \caption{Overview of a direct torque control system for a PMSM (the reference flux linkage $\|\bm{\psi}_{\mathrm{s}}\|^*$ can be directly obtained from the previously introduced OPS, e.g., from \figref{fig:LUT_OPS})}
        \label{fig:dtc_SM_high_level}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Mapping elementary voltage vectors toward flux changes %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}[b]
    \frametitle{Mapping elementary voltage vectors toward flux and torque changes}
    \vspace{0.3em}
    \begin{columns}[T,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.52\textwidth}
            Historically the DTC scheme was applied to SPMSM drives without magnetic saturation. Hence, the simplified flux model $$
                \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}(t) = L_\mathrm{s}\bm{i}_\mathrm{s}(t) + \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM}$$ with $L_\mathrm{dd}=L_\mathrm{qq}=L_\mathrm{s}$ and $L_\mathrm{dq}=L_\mathrm{qd}=0$ was used. \onslide<2->{In this case, the torque simplifies to}
            \begin{align*}
                \onslide<2->{\bm{T} & = \nicefrac{3}{2} p (\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}(t))\T\bm{J}\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s,dq}(t)              \\}
                \onslide<3->{& = \nicefrac{3}{2} \nicefrac{p}{L_\mathrm{s}} (\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM})\T\bm{J}\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s,dq}(t)                \\}
                \onslide<4->{& = \nicefrac{3}{2} \nicefrac{p}{L_\mathrm{s}} \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM}\| \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s,dq}(t)\| \sin(\delta(t))}
            \end{align*}
            \onslide<4->{where $\delta(t)$ is the angle between the stator flux and the PM flux.}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \centering
            \vspace{-0.275cm}
            \onslide<5->{
                    \begin{figure}
                        \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.25cm,y=1.25cm,>=Latex]
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{1}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaRadius}{\outerRadius*sin(60)}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisNegativeFactor}{1.25}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisPositiveFactor}{1.35}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaAxisFactor}{1.1}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPMr}{2.5}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPMNullgrad}{15}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPsgrad}{67.6}
                            \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPsr}{2.76}


                            \coordinate (psi0) at (\psiPsgrad:\psiPsr);
                            \coordinate (psiPM) at (\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPMr);
                            \fill[fill=gray!50] (0,0) -- (psi0) -- ($(psiPM) + (psi0)$) -- (psiPM) -- cycle;

                            \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                                    \coordinate (\name) at ($(\angle:\outerRadius) + (psi0)$);
                                }
                            \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\betaRadius);
                            \coordinate (alphaAxisStart) at (-0.75,0);
                            \coordinate (alphaAxisEnd) at (4,0);
                            \coordinate (betaAxisStart) at (0,-0.75);
                            \coordinate (betaAxisEnd) at (0,4);

                            \draw[->] (alphaAxisStart) -- (alphaAxisEnd) node[below] {$\upalpha$};
                            \draw[->] (betaAxisStart) -- (betaAxisEnd) node[left] {$\upbeta$};


                            \foreach \vertex in {u1,u2,u3,u4,u5,u6} {
                                    \draw[signalalpha,->,thick, dashed] (psi0) -- (\vertex);
                                }

                            \node[right] at (u1) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}1}$};
                            \node[above] at (u2) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}2}$};
                            \node[above] at (u3) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}3}$};
                            \node[left] at (u4) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}4}$};
                            %\node[below] at (u5) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}5}$};
                            \node[below] at (u6) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}6}$};

                            \fill[signalalpha] (psi0) circle (2pt);
                            \draw[thick, signalalpha, ->] (0,0) -- node[left, pos=0.5]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}$} (psi0);
                            \draw[thick, signaldelta, ->] (0,0) -- (psiPM) node[below, pos=0.75]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM}$};
