                            \draw[dashed] (psiPM) -- ($(psiPM) + (psi0)$);
                            \draw[dashed] (psi0) -- ($(psiPM) + (psi0)$);
                            \draw[thin] ($(psi0)!0.5!(psiPM) + (0.5,0)$) -- ++(0.8,-0.3) node[right] {$\sim T$};
                            \draw[->] (0,0) ++(\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPMr*0.4) arc (\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPsgrad:\psiPMr*0.4) node[pos=0.5, below left] {$\delta$};
                        \end{tikzpicture}
                        \caption{DTC control idea}
                        \label{fig:elementary_voltage_vectors_DTC_torque}
                    \end{figure}
                }
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Mapping elementary voltage vectors toward flux changes %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}[b]
    \frametitle{Mapping elementary voltage vectors toward flux changes in discrete time}
    \vspace{0.3em}
    \begin{columns}[T,onlytextwidth]
        \begin{column}{0.52\textwidth}
            When applying the DTC scheme in discrete time, the stator flux at the next sampling instant can be approximated as
            \begin{align*}
                \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}[k+1] & \approx \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}[k] + T_\mathrm{s} \left( \bm{u}_\mathrm{s}[k] - R_\mathrm{s}\bm{i}_\mathrm{s}[k] \right) \\
                                          & \approx \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}[k] + T_\mathrm{s} \bm{u}_\mathrm{s}[k].
            \end{align*}
            \onslide<2->{The latter neglects ohmic voltage drop allowing a direct mapping from applied voltage vector to the next stator flux vector.}
            \begin{itemize}
                \item<3-> Given some sampling time $T_\mathrm{s}$, only discrete flux vector changes are possible.
                \item<4-> Hence, $T_\mathrm{s}$ needs to be chosen sufficiently small to allow for a good control performance.
            \end{itemize}
        \end{column}
        \begin{column}{0.47\textwidth}
            \centering
            \vspace{-0.275cm}
            \begin{figure}
                \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.25cm,y=1.25cm,>=Latex]
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{1}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaRadius}{\outerRadius*sin(60)}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisNegativeFactor}{1.25}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisPositiveFactor}{1.35}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaAxisFactor}{1.1}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPMr}{2.5}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPMNullgrad}{5}
                    \pgfmathsetmacro{\psiPMEinsgrad}{15}

                    \coordinate (psi0) at (2.2,2.55);
                    \coordinate (psiPM0) at (\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPMr);
                    \coordinate (psiPM1) at (\psiPMEinsgrad:\psiPMr);
                    \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                            \coordinate (\name) at ($(\angle:\outerRadius) + (psi0)$);
                        }
                    \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\betaRadius);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisStart) at (-0.75,0);
                    \coordinate (alphaAxisEnd) at (4,0);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisStart) at (0,-0.75);
                    \coordinate (betaAxisEnd) at (0,4);

                    \draw[->] (alphaAxisStart) -- (alphaAxisEnd) node[below] {$\upalpha$};
                    \draw[->] (betaAxisStart) -- (betaAxisEnd) node[left] {$\upbeta$};


                    \foreach \vertex in {u1,u2,u3,u4,u5,u6} {
                            \draw[signalalpha,->,thick, dashed] (psi0) -- (\vertex);
                        }

                    \node[right] at (u1) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}1}$};
                    \node[above] at (u2) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}2}$};
                    \node[above] at (u3) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}3}$};
                    \node[left] at (u4) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}4}$};
                    \node[below] at (u5) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}5}$};
                    \node[below] at (u6) {$T_\mathrm{s}\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}6}$};

                    \fill[signalalpha] (psi0) circle (2pt);
                    \draw[thick, signalalpha, ->] (0,0) -- node[right, pos=0.3]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}[k]$} (psi0);
                    \draw[thick, signalalpha, ->] (0,0) -- node[left, pos=0.9]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}[k+1]$} (u3);
                    \draw[thick, signaldelta, ->] (0,0) -- (psiPM0) node[right]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM}[k]$};
                    \draw[thick, signaldelta, ->] (0,0) --  (psiPM1) node[right]{$\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{PM}[k+1]$};
                    \draw[->] (0,0) ++(\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPMr*0.8) arc (\psiPMNullgrad:\psiPMEinsgrad:\psiPMr*0.8);
                    \draw[thin] (\psiPMNullgrad/2+\psiPMEinsgrad/2:\psiPMr*0.75) -- ++(-0.2,-.35) node[below] {$\omega[k] T_\mathrm{s}$};
                \end{tikzpicture}
                \caption{Discrete time flux linkage change}
                \label{fig:elementary_voltage_vectors_DTC_discrete_time}
            \end{figure}
        \end{column}
    \end{columns}
\end{frame}



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DTC switching table %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{DTC switching table}

    \begin{table}[htbp]
        \centering
        \begin{tabular}{c c c c c c}
            \toprule
            Sector
              &
            \begin{tabular}[c]{@{}c@{}}
                $\Delta T > 0$ \\
                $\Delta \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}\| > 0$
            \end{tabular}
              &
            \begin{tabular}[c]{@{}c@{}}
                $\Delta T > 0$ \\
                $\Delta \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}\| < 0$
            \end{tabular}
              &
            \begin{tabular}[c]{@{}c@{}}
                $\Delta T < 0$ \\
                $\Delta \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}\| > 0$
            \end{tabular}
              &
            \begin{tabular}[c]{@{}c@{}}
                $\Delta T < 0$ \\
                $\Delta \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}\| < 0$
            \end{tabular}
              &
            \begin{tabular}[c]{@{}c@{}}
                $\Delta T < 0$ if $\omega > 0$ \\
                $\Delta T > 0$ if $\omega < 0$ \\
                $\Delta \|\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s}\| \approx 0$
            \end{tabular}
            \\
            \midrule
            1 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}3}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}6}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}5}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            2 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}3}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}4}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}6}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            3 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}4}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}5}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            4 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}5}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}6}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}3}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            5 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}6}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}4}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}3}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            6 & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}1}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}2}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}5}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}4}$ & $\bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}0}, \bm{s}_{\mathrm{i}7}$ \\
            \bottomrule
        \end{tabular}
        \caption{Exemplary DTC switching table\footnote{It should be noted that the switching strategy is not a unique choice. Depending on different control goals other switching tables might be more suited incl. a finer sector division and state-dependent strategies.} for different control situations}
        \label{tab:DTC_switching_table}
    \end{table}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DTC sector definition %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{DTC sector definition}
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1.25cm,y=1.25cm,>=Latex]
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\outerRadius}{2.2}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaRadius}{\outerRadius*sin(60)}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisNegativeFactor}{1.25}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaAxisPositiveFactor}{1.35}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaAxisFactor}{1.1}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\tickHalf}{0.08}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftX}{0.03}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderShiftY}{-0.15}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDx}{0.10}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\alphaLeaderDy}{-0.28}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftX}{0.08}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderShiftY}{0.08}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDx}{0.35}
            \pgfmathsetmacro{\betaLeaderDy}{0.20}

            \draw[dashed] (30:\outerRadius*1.1) -- (210:\outerRadius*1.1);
            \draw[dashed] (-30:\outerRadius*1.1) -- (150:\outerRadius*1.1);


            \coordinate (u0) at (0,0);
            \foreach \name/\angle in {u1/0,u2/60,u3/120,u4/180,u5/240,u6/300} {
                    \coordinate (\name) at (\angle:\outerRadius);
                }
            \coordinate (betaMax) at (90:\betaRadius);
            \coordinate (alphaAxisStart) at (180:{\alphaAxisNegativeFactor*\outerRadius});
            \coordinate (alphaAxisEnd) at (0:{\alphaAxisPositiveFactor*\outerRadius});
            \coordinate (betaAxisStart) at (270:{\betaAxisFactor*\outerRadius});
            \coordinate (betaAxisEnd) at (90:{\betaAxisFactor*\outerRadius});

            \draw[->,thin] (alphaAxisStart) -- (alphaAxisEnd) node[below] {$u_{\upalpha i}$};
            \draw[->,thin] (betaAxisStart) -- (betaAxisEnd) node[left] {$u_{\upbeta i}$};

            \draw[thin] (u1) ++(0,\tickHalf) -- ++(0,-2*\tickHalf);
            \draw[thin] ($(u1) + (\alphaLeaderShiftX,\alphaLeaderShiftY)$) -- ++(\alphaLeaderDx,\alphaLeaderDy) node[below right] {$\frac{2}{3}u_\mathrm{dc}$};

            \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,\betaLeaderShiftY) -- ++(\betaLeaderDx,\betaLeaderDy) node[above right] {$\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}u_\mathrm{dc}$};
            \draw[thin] (betaMax) ++(\betaLeaderShiftX,0) -- ++(-2*\betaLeaderShiftX,0);

            \foreach \vertex in {u1,u2,u3,u4,u5,u6} {
                    \draw[signalalpha,->,thick] (u0) -- (\vertex);
                }

            \foreach \sector/\angle in {1/0,2/60,3/120,4/180,5/240,6/300} {
                    \node[font=\footnotesize, fill=white, inner sep=1pt] at (\angle:\outerRadius*0.6) {Sector \sector};
                }

            \node[above right] at (u1) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}1}$};
            \node[above right] at (u2) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}2}$};
            \node[above left] at (u3) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}3}$};
            \node[above left] at (u4) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}4}$};
            \node[below left] at (u5) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}5}$};
            \node[below right] at (u6) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}6}$};

            \fill[signalalpha] (u0) circle (3pt);
            \node[below right, xshift=0.08cm] at (u0) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}7}$};
            \node[above right, xshift=0.08cm] at (u0) {$\bm{u}_{\mathrm{i}0}$};
        \end{tikzpicture}
        \caption{DTC sector definition (it should be noted that the DTC's sectors are different from the commonly used sectors for VSI modulation -- compare \figref{fig:elementary_voltages_alpha_beta}).}
        \label{fig:DTC_sector_definition}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% DTC switching frequency %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{DTC switching frequency}
    \begin{itemize}
        \item<1-> The switching frequency of the DTC scheme is not fixed but depends on the operating point and the chosen hysteresis band widths.
        \item<2-> This is a major difference compared to modulation-based control schemes where the switching frequency can be pre-defined.
        \item<3-> To achieve an average reference switching frequency of $f^*_\mathrm{s}$, the hysteresis band widths can be adapted online based on the observed switching actions $\Delta s_i = s_i[k] - s_i[k-1]$ for $i \in \{\mathrm{a},\mathrm{b},\mathrm{c}\}$.
    \end{itemize}
    \onslide<4->{
            \begin{figure}
                \begin{circuitikz}[x=1cm, y=1cm, scale=0.94, transform shape, >=Latex]
                    \def\stdgap{1.0cm}
                    \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}] (sumS) {};
                    \coordinate[left=\stdgap of sumS] (sumSInb);
                    \coordinate[above=\stdgap of sumSInb] (sumSIna);
                    \coordinate[below=\stdgap of sumSInb] (sumSInc);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumSInb)  node[above right]{$\Delta s_\mathrm{b}$} --  (sumS.west);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumSIna)  node[above right]{$\Delta s_\mathrm{a}$} -|  (sumS.north);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumSInc)  node[above right]{$\Delta s_\mathrm{c}$}-|  (sumS.south);
                    \node[signedmixer, right =1.5*\stdgap of sumS, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumF) {};
                    \coordinate[left=\stdgap of sumF] (sumFInAux);
                    \coordinate[below=\stdgap of sumFInAux] (sumFIn);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumFIn)  node[above right]{$3 f^*_\mathrm{s}$} -|  (sumF.south);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumS.east) -- (sumF.west);
                    \node[twoportshape, right=1.5*\stdgap of sumF, t=$\sum$] (int) {};
                    \draw[thick, ->] (sumF.east) -- (int.west);
                    \draw[thick] (int.east) to [short,-*] ++(\stdgap,0) coordinate (intOut);
                    \node[ctrlblock, right=2.5*\stdgap of int.north east, anchor=south] (Kt) {$K_T$};
                    \node[ctrlblock, right=2.5*\stdgap of int.south east, anchor=north] (Kpsi) {$K_\psi$};
                    \draw[thick, ->] (intOut) |- (Kt.west);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (intOut) |- (Kpsi.west);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (Kt.east)  -- node[above]{$\varepsilon_T$} ++(\stdgap,0);
                    \draw[thick, ->] (Kpsi.east)  -- node[above]{$\varepsilon_\psi$} ++(\stdgap,0);
                \end{circuitikz}
                \caption{Simplified (average) DTC switching frequency integral feedback control scheme}
                \label{fig:DTC_switching_frequency_control}
            \end{figure}}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsubsection{Flux linkage estimation}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Flux linkage estimation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Flux linkage estimation introduction}
    As discussed above, the DTC scheme relies on an accurate estimation of
    $$
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_\mathrm{s,\upalpha\upbeta} \approx \bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s,\upalpha\upbeta}.
    $$\pause%
    For this task we will review three \hl{open-loop flux estimation} methods:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Current moodel \pause%
        \item Voltage model \pause%
        \item Gopinath estimator (combined current and voltage model)\pause%
    \end{itemize}
    While not explicitly covered in this lecture, classical \hl{closed-loop observers} such as the \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_observer}{Luenberger observer} and the \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalman_filter}{Kalman filter} can also be applied, e.g., based on the standard model \eqref{eq:basic_PMSM_model_set_RK1}. \pause \hl {Adverse effects} to be considered in this context include:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Parameter uncertainties (e.g., stator resistance) and model mismatches (e.g., due to magnetic saturation in a linear model approach), \pause%
        \item Measurement noise, offset and linearity errors.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Current model-based flux estimation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Current model-based flux estimation}
    Similarly to the FOC case, we assume a known stator currents to stator flux linkage mapping
    $$
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k]  = \hat{\bm{f}}_{\psi_\mathrm{s}}(\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k], \psi_\mathrm{PM}),
    $$
    e.g., due to a prior machine characterization. \pause Using inverse Park transformation, the stator flux in $\upalpha\upbeta$-coordinates can be estimated as
    $$
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_\mathrm{s,\upalpha\upbeta}[k]  = \bm{T}_\mathrm{p}(\varepsilon[k]) \hat{\bm{f}}_{\psi_\mathrm{s}}(\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}[k], \psi_\mathrm{PM}).
    $$\pause%
    Hence, this method relies on:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Rotor angle information (i.e., requires a rotor position sensor or an additional observer for angle estimation), \pause%
        \item An accurate machine model (e.g., including saturation effects), and \pause%
        \item An accurate current measurements.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Voltage model-based flux estimation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Voltage model-based flux estimation}
    The voltage model is based upon the stator flux dynamics in $\upalpha\upbeta$-coordinates
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t) = \int_{t_0}^t \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) - R_\mathrm{s}\,\bm{i}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) \, \mathrm{d}\tau + \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t_0)
    \end{equation}\pause%
    or directly in discrete time using explicit Euler method
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}[k+1] = \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}[k] + T_\mathrm{s}\left(\bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}[k] - R_\mathrm{s}\,\bm{i}_{\upalpha\upbeta}[k]\right).
    \end{equation}\pause%
    While the rotor angle information and a fully fledged machine characterization are not required, this method relies on:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Accurate voltage information (e.g., based on precise inverter model or measurements), \pause
        \item Knowledge of the stator resistance, and \pause
        \item An accurate current measurement.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Voltage model-based flux estimation (cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Voltage model-based flux estimation (cont.)}
    Consider any \hl{constant voltage offset} $\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}\neq 0$, e.g., due to an inverter non-linearity or a measurement error. \pause This will lead to a linearly increasing flux estimation error over time
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t) = \int_{t_0}^t \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) + \Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta} - R_\mathrm{s}\,\bm{i}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) \, \mathrm{d}\tau + \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t_0) = \bm{\psi}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t) + t\,\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence, over time the flux estimation will diverge and the closed-loop control will fail. A common solution to this problem is to apply a \hl{low-pass filtered integrator}
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t) = \int_{t_0}^t \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) + \Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta} - R_\mathrm{s}\,\bm{i}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(\tau) - \frac{1}{\tau}\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(t) \, \mathrm{d}\tau
    \end{equation}
    with the time constant $\tau$. \pause Interpreting $\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}$ as output, $\bm{u}'_{\upalpha\upbeta}= \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta} - R_\mathrm{s}\,\bm{i}_{\upalpha\upbeta}$ as input and $\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}$ as a disturbance, the estimated flux can be expressed in the Laplace domain\footnote{A digital implementation of the estimator would of course require a discrete-time representation. However, a simplified Laplace analysis is used for the following high-level discussion for sake of brevity.} as
    \begin{equation}
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) = \frac{1}{s + \frac{1}{\tau}}\bm{u}'_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) + \frac{1}{s + \frac{1}{\tau}}\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s).
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Voltage model-based flux estimation (cont.) %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Voltage model-based flux estimation (cont.)}
    The true flux can be expressed in the Laplace domain as
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{\psi}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) = \frac{1}{s}\bm{u}'_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s).
    \end{equation} \pause%
    Hence, the low-pass integrated voltage model's \hl{flux estimation error} results in
    \begin{equation}
        \begin{split}
            \Delta \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) = \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) - \bm{\psi}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) & = -\frac{\frac{1}{\tau}}{s+\frac{1}{\tau}}\frac{1}{s}\bm{u}'_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) + \frac{1}{s + \frac{1}{\tau}}\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) \\                                                                                                        & =\frac{-1}{s\tau+1}\bm{\psi}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s) + \frac{\tau}{s\tau + 1}\Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}(s).
        \end{split}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    From these transfer elements we can observe two conflicting design aspects:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item The voltage offset error is now bounded by $\tau \Delta \bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}$, i.e., the smaller $\tau$ the smaller the error. \pause%
        \item The estimation error is depending on the true flux in a low-pass filtered manner, i.e., for $\omega \gg \nicefrac{1}{\tau}$ the estimation error is small. Hence, the larger $\tau$ the higher the suitable speed range of the estimator.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation}
    \centering
    \begin{figure}
        \begin{circuitikz}[>=Latex, scale=0.75, transform shape]
            \tikzset{
                detailblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.34cm, minimum height=1.02cm, font=\small},
                intblock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.10cm, minimum height=1.02cm, font=\small},
                tfblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=2.00cm, minimum height=1.90cm, inner sep=0pt},
                dublock/.style = {ctrlblock, align=center, minimum width=1.72cm, minimum height=1.48cm, font=\small},
                satblock/.style = {draw, rectangle, thick, minimum width=1.64cm, minimum height=1.98cm, inner sep=0pt},
                sig/.style = {font=\small, inner sep=1.5pt},
                tap/.style = {circle, fill=black, inner sep=1.15pt}
            }
            \ctikzset{block left anchors pos=0.7, block right anchors pos=0.7}
            \def\phaseport{0.72}
            \def\smallgap{0.6cm}
            \def\medgap{1.0cm}
            \def\biggap{2.25cm}

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$-$}] (sumd) {};

            \node[detailblock, right=\medgap of sumd] (kpd) {$K_{\mathrm{p,g}}$};
            \coordinate[above=\smallgap of kpd] (kid);

            \draw[->, thick] (sumd) -- (kpd);

            \node[detailblock, below=\smallgap of kpd] (intd) {$\dfrac{\mathrm{z}T_\mathrm{s}}{\mathrm{z}-1}$};
            \draw[->, thick] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) to[short, *-] ($(sumd.east)!0.4!(kpd.west)$) |-  (intd.west);

            \node[detailblock, right=\smallgap of intd] (kid2) {$K_{\mathrm{i,g}}$};
            \draw[->, thick] (intd.east) -- (kid2.west);

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$}, tripoles/signedmixer/south={$+$},  tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}, right = \biggap of kpd] (sumvd) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (kid2.east) -| (sumvd.south);
            \draw[->, thick] (kpd.east) -- (sumvd.west);

            \node[detailblock, left=\biggap of sumd] (Tp1) {$T_{\mathrm{p}}(\varepsilon)$};
            \draw[->, thick] (Tp1) -- node[above, pos=0.35]{$\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{CM}}$} (sumd.west);
            \node[detailblock, left=\medgap of Tp1] (fpsi) {$f_{\psi_\mathrm{s}}(\cdot)$};
            \coordinate[below=\smallgap of Tp1] (eps);
            \draw[->, thick] (eps) -- node[right, near start]{$\varepsilon$} (Tp1.south);
            \draw[->, thick] (fpsi) -- node[above]{$\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$} (Tp1.west);

            \coordinate[left=\biggap of fpsi] (isdq);
            \draw[->, thick] (isdq) -- node[above, near start]{$\bm{i}_{\mathrm{s,dq}}$} (fpsi.west);
            \node[detailblock, above=\smallgap of kpd] (Rs) {$R_\mathrm{s}$};

            \node[signedmixer, tripoles/signedmixer/west={$+$},tripoles/signedmixer/north={$+$}, at = (Rs -| sumvd.north)] (sumui) {};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumui.south) -- node[right]{$\bm{u}'_{\upalpha\upbeta}$}(sumvd.north);
            \coordinate[above=\medgap of sumui] (us);
            \draw[->, thick] (us) -- node[right]{$\bm{u}_{\upalpha\upbeta}$}(sumui.north);
            \draw[->, thick] (Rs.east) -- (sumui.west);
            \draw[->, thick] ($(isdq)!0.5!(fpsi.west)$) to[short, *-] ($(isdq)!0.5!(fpsi.west)$) |- (Rs.west);
            \node[detailblock, right=\medgap of sumvd] (intpsi) {$\dfrac{\mathrm{z}T_\mathrm{s}}{\mathrm{z}-1}$};
            \draw[->, thick] (sumvd.east) -- (intpsi.west);
            \coordinate[right=\biggap of intpsi] (psiout);
            \draw[->, thick] (intpsi) -- node[above]{$\hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{VM}}$}(psiout);
            \coordinate[below=1.25*\biggap of $(intpsi.east)!0.5!(psiout)$] (aux);
            \draw[->, thick] ($(intpsi.east)!0.5!(psiout)$) to [short, *- ] (aux) -| (sumd.south);
            \node[draw, dashed,fit=(isdq) ($(Tp1.east)!0.75!(sumd.west)$) (isdq) (fpsi) (Tp1)] (fitCM) {};
            \node[below, anchor=north west] at (fitCM.south west) {Current model};
            % --- Voltage-model boundary -------------------------------
            \def\vmpad{0.25cm}

            % common horizontal/vertical reference coordinates
            \coordinate (vmTopY)    at ($(us)+(0,\vmpad)$);
            \coordinate (vmBottomY) at ($(intpsi.south)+(0,-\vmpad)$);

            \coordinate (vmLeftX)  at ($(Rs.north west)+(-\vmpad*1.5,0)$);
            \coordinate (vmRightX) at ($(psiout)+(\vmpad,0)$);

            % outer corners with exactly equal top y-coordinate
            \coordinate (vmNW) at (vmLeftX  |- vmTopY);
            \coordinate (vmNE) at (vmRightX |- vmTopY);
            \coordinate (vmSE) at (vmRightX |- vmBottomY);

            % notch position
            \coordinate (vmStepY) at ($(Rs.south)!0.55!(kpd.north)$);
            \coordinate (vmStepX) at ($(sumvd.west)+(-0.35cm,0)$);

            % notch corners
            \coordinate (vmA) at (vmLeftX  |- vmStepY);
            \coordinate (vmB) at (vmStepX  |- vmStepY);
            \coordinate (vmC) at (vmStepX  |- vmBottomY);

            % draw the notched voltage-model box
            \draw[draw, dashed, thick]
            (vmNW) -- (vmNE) -- (vmSE) -- (vmC) -- (vmB) -- (vmA) -- cycle;

            % label
            \node[anchor=north east] at (vmNE) {Voltage model};
            \node[anchor=north west, xshift = 0.3cm] at (kpd.south west) {PI controller};


        \end{circuitikz}%
        \caption{Gopinath observer combining the current model for low-speed operation and the voltage model for high-speed operation with a PI controller managing the transition between the two models. Below the PI's cut off frequency, the current model is dominant (i.e., the voltage model's output is suppressed by the current model), while above the cutoff frequency, the voltage model is largely unaffected.}
        \label{fig:Gopinath_PMSM}
    \end{figure}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: loop transfer
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based transfer function}
    Consider the feedback path from the current-model flux linkage estimate to the voltage-model flux linkage estimate while the voltage feedforward input is neglected:
    \begin{equation}
        \bm{e}_\psi
        =
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{CM}}
        -
        \hat{\bm{\psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{VM}} .
    \end{equation}\pause%
    With the discrete-time PI correction element and the voltage-model integrator
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{c,g}}(\mathrm{z})
        =K_{\mathrm{p,g}}
        +K_{\mathrm{i,g}}T_\mathrm{s}\frac{\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-1},
        \qquad
        G_{\mathrm{VM}}(\mathrm{z})
        =T_\mathrm{s}\frac{\mathrm{z}}{\mathrm{z}-1},
    \end{equation}\pause%
    the open-loop transfer function of the Gopinath correction path is
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\mathrm{o,g}}(\mathrm{z})
        =G_{\mathrm{VM}}(\mathrm{z})G_{\mathrm{c,g}}(\mathrm{z}).
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The closed-loop transfer function is then
    \begin{equation}
        G_{\psi,\mathrm{g}}(\mathrm{z})
        =
        \frac{\hat{\bm{\Psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{VM}}(\mathrm{z})}
        {\hat{\bm{\Psi}}_{\upalpha\upbeta,\mathrm{CM}}(\mathrm{z})}
        =
        \frac{G_{\mathrm{o,g}}(\mathrm{z})}{1+G_{\mathrm{o,g}}(\mathrm{z})} =
        \frac{\mathrm{z}\left[(a+b)\mathrm{z}-a\right]}
        {(1+a+b)\mathrm{z}^2-(2+a)\mathrm{z}+1}
        \label{eq:gopinath_closed_loop_transfer_function}
    \end{equation}
    with the dimensionless gains
    \begin{equation}
        a=K_{\mathrm{p,g}}T_\mathrm{s},
        \qquad
        b=K_{\mathrm{i,g}}T_\mathrm{s}^2.
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: poles and zeros
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation: poles and zeros}
    From \eqref{eq:gopinath_closed_loop_transfer_function}, the zeros are
    \begin{equation}
        z_{\psi,1}=0,
        \qquad
        z_{\psi,2}
        =\frac{a}{a+b}
        =\frac{K_{\mathrm{p,g}}}{K_{\mathrm{p,g}}+K_{\mathrm{i,g}}T_\mathrm{s}} .
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The closed-loop poles are denoted by $\lambda$ and follow from the characteristic polynomial
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta_\psi(\mathrm{z})
        =(1+a+b)\mathrm{z}^2-(2+a)\mathrm{z}+1.
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Hence,
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{1,2}
        =
        \frac{2+a\pm\sqrt{a^2-4b}}{2(1+a+b)} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: PI design
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation: PI design}
    A direct discrete-time pole-placement design chooses desired poles $\lambda_1$ and $\lambda_2$ and matches
    \begin{equation}
        \Delta_\psi(\mathrm{z})
        =(1+a+b)(\mathrm{z}-\lambda_1)(\mathrm{z}-\lambda_2).
    \end{equation}\pause%
    With
    \begin{equation}
        S_\lambda=\lambda_1+\lambda_2,
        \qquad
        P_\lambda=\lambda_1\lambda_2,
    \end{equation}\pause%
    coefficient matching gives
    \begin{equation}
        a=\frac{S_\lambda}{P_\lambda}-2,
        \qquad
        b=\frac{1-S_\lambda}{P_\lambda}+1 .
        \label{eq:gopinath_discrete_pole_placement_addendum}
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The PI gains are then obtained from
    \begin{equation}
        K_{\mathrm{p,g}}=\frac{a}{T_\mathrm{s}},
        \qquad
        K_{\mathrm{i,g}}=\frac{b}{T_\mathrm{s}^2} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: cutoff frequency decision
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation: cutoff-frequency decision}
    The design poles can be linked to a continuous-time second-order prototype by using
    \begin{equation}
        \lambda_{1,2}=\mathrm{e}^{s_{1,2}T_\mathrm{s}},
        \qquad
        s_{1,2}=-\zeta\omega_\mathrm{g}
        \pm\iu\omega_\mathrm{g}\sqrt{1-\zeta^2}
        \quad (0<\zeta<1),
    \end{equation}\pause%
    and the corresponding real-pole expression for $\zeta\geq 1$:
    \begin{equation}
        s_{1,2}=\omega_\mathrm{g}\left(-\zeta\pm\sqrt{\zeta^2-1}\right)
        \quad (\zeta\geq 1).
    \end{equation}\pause%
    The normalized digital design frequency is
    \begin{equation}
        \Omega_\mathrm{g}=\omega_\mathrm{g}T_\mathrm{s},
        \qquad
        \rho_\mathrm{g}=\frac{\Omega_\mathrm{g}}{\pi} .
    \end{equation}\pause%
    Design interpretation:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Smaller $\Omega_\mathrm{g}$ shifts the current-model-to-voltage-model transition to lower frequencies and increases high-frequency attenuation.\pause%
        \item Larger $\Omega_\mathrm{g}$ makes the observer follow the current model more broadly, but attenuates high-frequency components less.\pause%
        \item Larger $\zeta$ reduces peaking around the transition but increases phase lag.
    \end{itemize}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: selected designs
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

% Analytic frequency-response functions for
% G_{\psi,\mathrm{g}}(z)=z[(a+b)z-a]/[(1+a+b)z^2-(2+a)z+1]
% evaluated at z=exp(j*Omega), rho=Omega/pi.
\pgfmathdeclarefunction{GgPsiMagdB}{3}{%
    \pgfmathparse{%
        10*log10(%
        (((#1+#2)*cos(360*(#3))-(#1)*cos(180*(#3)))^2%
        +((#1+#2)*sin(360*(#3))-(#1)*sin(180*(#3)))^2)%
        /%
        (((1+#1+#2)*cos(360*(#3))-(2+#1)*cos(180*(#3))+1)^2%
        +((1+#1+#2)*sin(360*(#3))-(2+#1)*sin(180*(#3)))^2)%
        )%
    }%
}


% Phase of the same transfer function.  For numerical robustness inside PGF,
% the polynomial is evaluated with q=z-1 instead of z directly:
% N(q)=b+(a+2b)q+(a+b)q^2,
% D(q)=b+(a+2b)q+(1+a+b)q^2.
% The common scaling factor in atan2 prevents fixed-point underflow.
\pgfmathdeclarefunction{GgPsiPhaseDeg}{3}{%
    \pgfmathparse{%
        mod(%
        atan2(%
        1000*((#1+2*#2)*sin(180*(#3))%
        +2*(#1+#2)*(cos(180*(#3))-1)*sin(180*(#3))),%
        1000*(#2+(#1+2*#2)*(cos(180*(#3))-1)%
        +(#1+#2)*((cos(180*(#3))-1)^2-sin(180*(#3))^2))%
        )%
        - atan2(%
        1000*((#1+2*#2)*sin(180*(#3))%
        +2*(1+#1+#2)*(cos(180*(#3))-1)*sin(180*(#3))),%
        1000*(#2+(#1+2*#2)*(cos(180*(#3))-1)%
        +(1+#1+#2)*((cos(180*(#3))-1)^2-sin(180*(#3))^2))%
        )%
        +180,360)-180%
    }%
}

% Selected pole-placement designs.  The variables \Omega_g=\omega_g T_s
% and \zeta are used to compute a=K_{p,g}T_s and b=K_{i,g}T_s^2.
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgZetaOne}{0.7}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgOmegaOne}{0.015}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgAOne}{2*exp(\GgZetaOne*\GgOmegaOne)*cos(\GgOmegaOne*sqrt(1-\GgZetaOne*\GgZetaOne)*180/pi)-2}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgBOne}{exp(2*\GgZetaOne*\GgOmegaOne)-2*exp(\GgZetaOne*\GgOmegaOne)*cos(\GgOmegaOne*sqrt(1-\GgZetaOne*\GgZetaOne)*180/pi)+1}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgLReOne}{exp(-\GgZetaOne*\GgOmegaOne)*cos(\GgOmegaOne*sqrt(1-\GgZetaOne*\GgZetaOne)*180/pi)}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgLImOne}{exp(-\GgZetaOne*\GgOmegaOne)*sin(\GgOmegaOne*sqrt(1-\GgZetaOne*\GgZetaOne)*180/pi)}

\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgZetaTwo}{1.0}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgOmegaTwo}{0.030}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgATwo}{2*exp(\GgOmegaTwo)-2}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgBTwo}{exp(2*\GgOmegaTwo)-2*exp(\GgOmegaTwo)+1}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgLTwo}{exp(-\GgOmegaTwo)}

\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgZetaThree}{1.5}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgOmegaThree}{0.060}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgRThree}{sqrt(\GgZetaThree*\GgZetaThree-1)}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgAThree}{exp(\GgOmegaThree*(\GgZetaThree+\GgRThree))+exp(\GgOmegaThree*(\GgZetaThree-\GgRThree))-2}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgBThree}{exp(2*\GgZetaThree*\GgOmegaThree)-exp(\GgOmegaThree*(\GgZetaThree+\GgRThree))-exp(\GgOmegaThree*(\GgZetaThree-\GgRThree))+1}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgLThreeOne}{exp(\GgOmegaThree*(-\GgZetaThree+\GgRThree))}
\pgfmathsetmacro{\GgLThreeTwo}{exp(\GgOmegaThree*(-\GgZetaThree-\GgRThree))}

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation: selected designs}
    The following designs vary both damping and transition frequency. The gains are calculated using the exact pole-placement relation in \eqref{eq:gopinath_discrete_pole_placement_addendum}.
    \begin{center}
        \begin{tabular}{cccc}
            \toprule
            $\zeta$                                              & $\Omega_\mathrm{g}$                                   & $a=K_{\mathrm{p,g}}T_\mathrm{s}$                  & $b=K_{\mathrm{i,g}}T_\mathrm{s}^2$                \\
            \midrule
            \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=1]{\GgZetaOne}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=3]{\GgOmegaOne}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=4]{\GgAOne}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=5]{\GgBOne}   \\
            \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=1]{\GgZetaTwo}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=3]{\GgOmegaTwo}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=4]{\GgATwo}   & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=5]{\GgBTwo}   \\
            \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=1]{\GgZetaThree} & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=3]{\GgOmegaThree} & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=4]{\GgAThree} & \pgfmathprintnumber[fixed,precision=5]{\GgBThree} \\
            \bottomrule
        \end{tabular}
    \end{center}\pause%
    The frequency response is evaluated at
    \begin{equation}
        \mathrm{z}=\mathrm{e}^{\iu\Omega},
        \qquad
        \rho=\frac{\Omega}{\pi}=\frac{\omega T_\mathrm{s}}{\pi}=\frac{2f}{f_\mathrm{s}} .
    \end{equation}
\end{frame}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Gopinath observer: Bode diagram
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Gopinath observer-based flux linkage estimation: Bode diagram}
    \begin{center}
        \begin{figure}
            \begin{tikzpicture}
                \begin{axis}[
                        name=magaxis,
                        width=0.92\textwidth,
                        height=0.42\textheight,
                        xmin=1e-4, xmax=1,
                        xmode=log,
                        ymin=-45, ymax=5,
                        grid=both,
                        ylabel={Magnitude in \si{\decibel}},
                        xticklabels=\empty,
                        legend columns=3,
                        legend style={
                                at={(0.5,1.18)},
                                anchor=south,
                                draw=none,
                                fill=none,
                                font=\footnotesize,
                                /tikz/every even column/.append style={column sep=0.6em}
                            }]
                    \addplot[signalalpha, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiMagdB(\GgAOne,\GgBOne,10^x)});
                    \addlegendentry{$\zeta=0.7$, $\Omega_\mathrm{g}=0.015$}
                    \addplot[signalbeta, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiMagdB(\GgATwo,\GgBTwo,10^x)});
                    \addlegendentry{$\zeta=1.0$, $\Omega_\mathrm{g}=0.030$}
                    \addplot[signaldelta, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiMagdB(\GgAThree,\GgBThree,10^x)});
                    \addlegendentry{$\zeta=1.5$, $\Omega_\mathrm{g}=0.060$}
                \end{axis}
                \begin{axis}[
                        at={(magaxis.south west)},
                        anchor=north west,
                        yshift=-0.55cm,
                        width=0.92\textwidth,
                        height=0.42\textheight,
                        xmin=1e-4, xmax=1,
                        xmode=log,
                        ymin=-90, ymax=5,
                        grid=both,
                        xlabel={Normalized digital frequency $\rho=\Omega/\pi$},
                        ylabel={Phase in \si{\degree}}]
                    \addplot[signalalpha, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiPhaseDeg(\GgAOne,\GgBOne,10^x)});
                    \addplot[signalbeta, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiPhaseDeg(\GgATwo,\GgBTwo,10^x)});
                    \addplot[signaldelta, thick, smooth, domain=-4:0, samples=300]
                    ({10^x},{GgPsiPhaseDeg(\GgAThree,\GgBThree,10^x)});
                \end{axis}
            \end{tikzpicture}
            \caption{Bode diagram for Gopinath observer with selected design examples}
            \label{fig:Gopinath_Bode}
        \end{figure}
    \end{center}
\end{frame}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Small comparison: FOC vs. DTC %%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{frame}
    \frametitle{Small comparison: FOC vs. DTC}
    \begin{table}
        \centering
        \small
        \renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
        \begin{tabular}{@{}p{3.75cm} P{5cm} P{5cm}}
            \toprule%
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    & \textbf{FOC}                                                             & \textbf{DTC}                                                           \\%
            \midrule%
            Controlled variables                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    & $\bm{i}_\mathrm{s,dq}$                                                   & $\bm{\psi}_\mathrm{s,\upalpha\upbeta}$ and $T$                         \\%
            Control actions                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         & $\bm{u}_\mathrm{s,dq}$ (per sample period average voltage for modulator) & $\bm{u}_\mathrm{s,\upalpha\upbeta}$ (direct inverter switching vector) \\%
            Relevant measurements\footnote{The stator voltage is typically estimated based on the nonlinear inverter model but could be also measured, which however, would require a very fast voltage measurement due to the inverter switching characteristics.} & $\bm{u}_\mathrm{s}, \bm{i}_\mathrm{s}, \varepsilon$                      & $\bm{u}_\mathrm{s}, \bm{i}_\mathrm{s}$                                 \\%
            Switching frequency                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     & Constant for any control period / inherently controllable                & Variable / only controllable in average over multiple periods          \\%
            Control rate                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            & Moderate due to regular sampling / modulator                             & Fast due to direct  inverter actuation                                 \\%
            Numerical effort                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        & Moderate (complex controllers, coordinate transf.)                       & Low (mostly simple hysteresis comparators)                             \\%
            \bottomrule%
        \end{tabular}
        \caption{Qualitative comparison of FOC vs. DTC}
        \label{tab:DTC_FOC_comparison}
    \end{table}
\end{frame}
